Two Memorial Weeks Held at the Central Government Yesterday 15

Vice Chairman Chiang: "Methods to Improve Work Efficiency"; Chairman Lin Reports on the Significance of "Peaceful Struggle to Save China"

Nanjing - The Central Government held its eleventh memorial week at 9:00 a.m. on the 17th. Vice Chairman Chiang and Central Committee members Lin Sen, Zhang Ji, Ye Chucang, Jing Hengyi, Jiang Zuobin, Chen Gongbo, Gu Zhenglun, Cheng Qian, Chen Shuren, Sun Ke, Ju Zheng, Gan Naiguang, He Yingqin, Chen Shaokuan, Chen Ce, Ma Chaojun, Fang Zhi, Li Zonghuang, and Zhou Qigang, as well as Yao Dahai and more than 60 other people, attended. Vice Chairman Chiang presided over the meeting, and Ye Chucang gave a report. Vice Chairman Chiang delivered a speech, both giving instructions on the party affairs work policy. (17th Central News Agency Dispatch)

Nanjing - Chairman Lin reported on "Peaceful Struggle to Save China" at the National Government Memorial Week on the morning of the 17th. He explained in great detail the points according to the Prime Minister's teachings, meaning that "Peaceful Struggle to Save China" was the Prime Minister's last teaching. We should never forget it. The Prime Minister's lifelong spirit and purpose was to save China, so the struggle is for saving China, and peace is for saving China. We should struggle when we should struggle, and we should have peace when we should have peace. Our revolution is to convince people with virtue and with ideology, not with force. The country is currently in distress, and I hope everyone will always remember peace and not forget the struggle, in order to achieve the true goal of saving China. (16th Central News Agency Dispatch)

Nanjing - The National Government held a memorial week at 10:00 a.m. on the 17th. Chen Shaokuan, Chen Shuren, Deng Jiayan, Chen Xunyong, Lü Chao, Wei Huai, Chen Qicai, and other officials from various departments and committees of the National Government, totaling more than 400 people, attended. After Chairman Lin led the ceremony, he gave an impromptu report entitled "Peaceful Struggle to Save China." The meeting ended at 10:30 a.m. (17th Central News Agency Dispatch)

Nanjing - Vice Chairman Chiang delivered a speech at the Central Party Headquarters Memorial Week on the morning of the 17th, entitled "Methods to Improve Work Efficiency." The original text is as follows: Fellow comrades, Mr. Ye Chucang just gave a report on recent party affairs, and finally emphasized the two points of "management" and "performance appraisal." I feel that if these two points can be done effectively, they will be very important for the future work efficiency and factual development of our party headquarters and general party members. Therefore, after Mr. Ye's report, I will briefly report a few of my personal opinions to everyone. Everyone often feels that our party has no spirit, only a shell, and is not an ideal revolutionary party. Therefore, all work cannot be promoted according to our plan. Why is this happening? Chinese people are people, and foreigners are also people. Why can foreigners organize a party that is spirited and persevering, while our party, although its spirit is good at first, inevitably becomes lax and disorganized later? I think the biggest reason is that our general superiors and comrades who have leadership responsibilities, from committee members and ministers to section chiefs and section leaders, have not fulfilled their responsibilities. They have not paid attention to training their subordinates, or the training is not effective. We must know that whether it is party affairs, politics, or military affairs, they can only be promoted smoothly if our general supervisors and officials can not only know people and be good at their jobs, but also train their subordinates at any time to cultivate talents. Therefore, superiors should not only direct their subordinates to do things, but also train them so that their knowledge, talents, spirit, and character can continue to improve. They must also increase their experience and ability in personnel management, that is, supervising, directing, and teaching subordinates, as well as the general public, so that all work can not only be gradually promoted, but also always have suitable talents who can continue to be responsible for it. The general situation now is that this point is not fully achieved, so our party cannot be spirited and quickly promote various revolutionary tasks. We learn from the past and hope that the general comrades who bear the responsibility of supervision will pay special attention to training their subordinates in the future. Of course, if we want to train people, we must first train ourselves. We must also be able to supervise ourselves before we can supervise others. If we want to fulfill the responsibility of superiors to train subordinates, we must first be able to lead by example in everything. At the same time, the general comrades who handle affairs must also be aware, automatically invigorate their spirits, and strive for progress. Everyone must recognize that our office is a school, and the superiors are the teachers in this school, and the general subordinates are the students. We must all, from top to bottom, be based on the principle of "organizing schools" and "work educating," and strive together. Then, the efficiency of handling affairs can be greatly improved, and the "management" that Mr. Ye just mentioned can be said to be done perfectly. Finally, as Mr. Ye has already mentioned, "performance appraisal" is the most important thing to improve work efficiency and train subordinates. However, in order for performance appraisal to achieve satisfactory results, it must be able to use reasonable and practical methods. This method must of course be studied and determined according to the situation of each agency and the work of each person, and cannot be generalized. However, there is one point that I think is very important: whether we train or evaluate our subordinates, it is best to call each of them to draft plans to promote work or solve problems within the scope of their responsibilities or for practical problems directly related to their responsibilities. Moreover, for each matter or each problem, it is best to predetermine a variety of different plans based on various possible situations, rather than just one plan. In this way, first, it can enable general subordinates to often exert their intelligence and talents to plan their own work and deal with current problems, so as to cultivate their thorough thinking, automatic spirit, and creative ability, and achieve our goal of training subordinates and cultivating talents. Second, by reviewing the plans they have drafted, we can know how smart and talented each subordinate is, how much experience and knowledge they have, and we can also recognize their thoughts, spirit, and even character. This is the most reasonable and practical method of performance appraisal. Third, it is necessary for us to do things well to establish more plans, because as a result of modern science and civilization progress, all aspects of society are unusually complex and constantly changing. It can be said that there is no one thing or one problem that can be done well by only determining one fixed situation and preparing a rigid plan. Therefore, in order to be able to do things well now, we must first study in detail the relationship between the things we do and all aspects of things, and then predict various possible situations and formulate various practical plans. Then, we can use the most appropriate plan at any time according to the actual situation. For example, if this matter encounters the first situation, we will use the first plan. If it is the second situation, we will use the second plan. It can also be said that if the first plan does not work for us to do this matter, we will use the second plan. If the second plan does not work, we will take out the third plan, and so on. In general, we must use the most appropriate plan to achieve the greatest effect and achieve the greatest success. The meaning of the above is that the first point is to pay attention to training subordinates, and the second point is to be able to establish more plans in handling affairs. I think these two points are the most important methods for us to improve work efficiency and exert revolutionary power in the future. Therefore, I have specially brought them up today to report to you. (17th Central News Agency Dispatch)

Unification Public Bond Exchange Date Set by Ministry of Finance 16

Nanjing: The Ministry of Finance has set the dates for exchanging Unification Public Bonds. Starting from March 11th, each of the five types (A, B, C, D, and E) will be exchanged for ten days each. The new public bond forms will be printed and completed by the end of the month. The Public Bond Department has drafted detailed exchange procedures, which have been communicated to the finance departments/bureaus and chambers of commerce in all provinces and cities, as well as to the silver and banking guilds, for compliance. The exchange will be handled by the Central Bank, the Bank of China, the Bank of Communications, and their branches in various locations. (17th dispatch)

The provincial government has ordered the counties to expedite relief efforts and resettle displaced persons. The total public and private losses in various counties amount to over ten million, with more than four thousand houses burned down. (17th dispatch)

Increase in Coolies Entering Customs 36

Beiping: Every spring, there is a constant stream of coolies leaving customs. According to an investigation by the authorities, the current daily average is 400 people. In January, there were only 3,000 people. Last January, there were a total of 20,000 people. However, the number of coolies entering customs is as high as 700 to 800 per day. The reason is that the order in various places outside the customs is unstable. (17th dispatch)

◎Madrid: The results of the House of Representatives elections as of now show the following number of seats won by each party: 120 seats for the right-wing Popular Action party led by former Minister of War Robles; 12 seats for the Agrarian Party; 2 seats for the Liberal Democratic Party; 34 seats for the Royalist Party; 2 seats for the Conservative Republican Party; 7 seats for the Catalan Autonomy Party; 16 seats for the Central Party; 16 seats for the Basque Nationalist Party (without affiliations); 10 seats for the Radical Party; and 200 seats for the Socialist Party, Republican Union Party, and Left Republican Party belonging to the left-wing Popular Front. ◎Madrid: Since the establishment of the Spanish Republic in 1931, the third parliamentary election was held today. It is noted that Catalonia is an autonomous province, and all political affairs, except for public security issues which are managed by the central government, are handled by the provincial government. Now that the left-wing has won, the autonomous nature will inevitably become more pronounced, which is a major problem for the central government. This is the reason why the Governor of the province, Escalar, submitted his resignation, and it was accepted by the Prime Minister Valladares. (Havas dispatch, 16th)

Although the vote counting in his constituency has not yet been completed as of the time of this dispatch, Valladares has only received 667 votes, while his political opponent among the left-wing candidates has already received 3,000 votes. In addition, the Minister of Labor and Justice, Piñeiro, the Minister of Foreign Affairs, Ussel, and the Minister of Education, Villalobos, are likely to be elected. The national election situation yesterday was very calm. Only in some places did the left and right wings hold demonstrations, with occasional disturbances, but they were immediately quelled, and the situation was not serious. Only in the cities of Zaragoza and La Coruña did one person die in each city. It is said that the leaders of the right-wing and central parties, especially the Popular Action party and the Royalist party, are all unhappy because the victory belongs to the left-wing. ◎Madrid: In this election for the House of Representatives, the left-wing parties formed a joint front called the "Popular Front" to compete with the right-wing. Qualitative Limitation of Naval Power: Experts Continue Meeting; The Battleship Issue Hinges on the Attitudes of France and Italy 49

London: The Subcommittee of Experts of the General Committee of the Naval Conference, responsible for drafting an agreement on the qualitative limitation of various warships (excluding battleships), held a meeting at Clarence House at 11:30 a.m. today, and is scheduled to continue the meeting this afternoon and tomorrow. Naval figures believe that the success or failure of the Naval Conference depends on the outcome of the French Ambassador to Britain, Corbin, and the Italian Naval Conference representatives, Lieutenant General Raineri and Rear Admiral Piccia, returning home for instructions. Regarding the issue of battleship tonnage, both France and Italy have raised objections to the 35,000 tons proposed by Britain and the United States. If this cannot be agreed upon, the previously agreed-upon issues of mutual notification of shipbuilding procedures and qualitative limitations of various auxiliary ships will all be in vain. Therefore, the representatives of the various countries will not hold important meetings before Corbin and Piccia return to London, and the two important issues of battleship tonnage and inviting Germany to participate in future agreements will also have to be discussed at a later date. (Havas dispatch, 17th)

First Major Battle Since the Battle of Magale: Italian Troops Win With New Weapons; Repel 80,000 Ethiopian Troops in Six Days of Fierce Fighting; Over a Thousand Killed and Wounded; Occupy 5,000-Foot-High Mountain; Approximately 5,000 Ethiopian Regular Army Soldiers Killed 50

◎Asmara: The first engagement between the Ethiopian regular army and the Italian army resulted in a major Italian victory. The Italian army has occupied Antalo, 15 miles south of Magale, and raised the Italian flag on Mount Amba Aradam. In this battle, 500 Italian soldiers were killed and 1,000 were wounded, while about 5,000 Ethiopian soldiers were killed. This was the first major battle since the Italian occupation of Magale, and the Italian victory is of great value. Mount Amba Aradam is 5,000 feet high and five miles wide, and is a natural barrier to the Sakota town on the highway to Taza. In this battle, various weapons of the new era, from hand grenades to airplanes, were used almost without exception, and it was the first battle in which all white soldiers participated. One division of Eritrean soldiers was only used as a reserve. The result was that the 25,000 regular troops led by Ethiopian General Mulugheta, who was holding Mount Amba Aradam, were driven away. The Ethiopian army also had 50,000 soldiers holding solid positions behind the defense to help. In this battle, the artillery played a great role. The horse artillery followed closely behind the Italian infantry, and the shells fired by the heavy artillery reached enemy positions ten miles away. However, tank artillery vehicles did not participate in the battle due to the inconvenient terrain. The battle was greatly hindered by continuous heavy rain. The Italian strategy was to have two independent columns bypass the eastern and western slopes of Amba Aradam and meet behind the mountain to encircle the mountain. It began on February 10. The First Army moved south to the Geba River, crossed the river safely without being seen by the enemy. The next day, the army captured the eastern edge of Amba Aradam, a mountain commonly known as Priest's Hat. On February 12, the First Division of the Third Army crossed the Battle River and reached a peak west of Amba Aradam at 8 a.m. The Ethiopian army put up fierce resistance. After that, intermittent shelling occurred, and the sound of artillery and aircraft rumbled, and the thatched huts were burned by the shells, with fires breaking out from time to time. Until 2:30 p.m., the heavy rain stopped the battle. At the same time, the left wing of the Blackshirts, who ascended the slope of Mount Amba Aradam, encountered strong resistance from the Ethiopian army. The Ethiopian army dispatched its entire reserve army to participate in the battle, repeatedly attacking Priest's Hat Mountain, aided by the artillery on Takoro, bombarding the Italian machine gun nests, but was eventually silenced by the Italian artillery's counter-bombardment. At noon, Italian Commander-in-Chief General Badoglio used Alpine Brigade troops to reinforce the battle. The battle lasted until 5 p.m., when the Italian army attacked its destination, the ridge of Mount Amba Aradam. On February 13, the Italian army began to repair the captured positions. The battle was greatly hampered by heavy rain, but 2,500 Ethiopian troops still attacked the Italian left wing in the rain, surrounding a large unit of the Sappada Division. The division relied on the help of the artillery to break through, killing 4,000 Ethiopian soldiers. Eighteen Italian soldiers were killed and sixty-four were wounded. On February 14, Italian aircraft braved the heavy rain to bombard the Ethiopian reinforcements that were moving from the rear to the front lines. On February 15, the Italian army advanced again on both flanks. The Ethiopian army resisted desperately. The Italian soldiers and machine guns on Mount Amba Aradam were all involved in the battle. The Italian artillery heavily bombarded the Ethiopian positions. At dusk, a team of Blackshirts, led by the Duke of Pistoia, raised the Italian flag on the summit of Mount Amba Aradam. The enemy troops retreated in the dark. Eventually, the Italian two-wing columns also met in Antalo, and saw enemy corpses lying everywhere, a testament to the ferocity of the Italian artillery bombardment. (Reuters dispatch, 17th)

◎Magale: According to news from our reporter, the Emba Aradam area captured by the Italian army a few days ago is located in the triangular area between Magale, Emba Lachi, and Donchian, with the highest terrain controlling the pass of Bojella Agathe. It is the only way from the Tambien area to the city of Taza where the Ethiopian Emperor resides. A large force of Ethiopian troops was concentrated there, personally led by General Mulugheta, the Minister of the Army of the regiment, and fortifications were built to serve as a barrier to the northern route. Mulugheta was originally a servant of the Emperor and has risen to his current position. The troops he leads are all official Ethiopian troops, with the majority being guards in yellow uniforms, carrying submachine guns, and fully supplied and armed. The officers all carry maps. On the Italian side, a total of five divisions participated in the battle, all of which were domestic troops with sophisticated equipment and airfields built in the vicinity to serve as bases for the air force. However, because the Ethiopian army had more personnel and was familiar with the local terrain, the strength of both sides was roughly equal. Previously, on the 11th of this month, Italian Commander-in-Chief General Badoglio believed that the Ethiopian army had attacked in the Tambien area without success and that it was advisable to take the opportunity to counterattack, so he immediately ordered an offensive to be launched on the Entelda Plateau. After fierce resistance, 30,000 Ethiopian soldiers retreated, and the Italian army took advantage of the victory to advance to the Emba Aradam area and engage in a major battle with the Ethiopian army. Late on the 14th, Ethiopian General Mulugheta was unable to hold on and withdrew his troops, and the area was occupied by the Italian army. After hearing the news of the victory at the command post's observation deck, General Badoglio issued a statement to the military reporters from various countries, saying, "The Emba Aradam area was captured after you arrived here. You have brought good luck with you. I have been uneasy about Emba Aradam not yet being captured for a long time. Now that the Italian flag is flying over the area, I can finally rest assured." The General then praised the Ethiopian army for being brave and good at fighting, and said that during the battle, there was continuous heavy rain, and the roadbeds were loose, making it very inconvenient for the Italian army to supply. The expeditionary force's staff headquarters also issued a statement saying that the victory in this battle was of great importance because the Italian army could take advantage of the victory to advance south. When the Ethiopian army retreated, they set fire to several villages and towns where they had stored food, such as Enema Lian, Baruto, and Guwossa. In general, although the Ethiopian army has mostly retreated, the Emba Aradam Plateau is vast, and it is possible that several thousand remaining troops are hiding in it. The Italian staff headquarters is concerned that the remaining troops will rejoin the Ethiopian army and launch attacks, so it ordered the burning of several villages and towns to clear them out. According to our reporter, after the Emba Aradam battle, large-scale military operations on the northern route seem to have come to an end, because the newly built roads are cut off in two places, the roadbeds are loose, and it is inconvenient for transportation, so it is inevitable that the march will be temporarily suspended. In addition, the military reporters from various countries who participated in the funeral of the fallen Blackshirts in the Serico area saw that many native soldiers had been hit by expanding bullets, with mutilated limbs, which was a tragic sight. (Havas dispatch, 16th)

Regarding the Issue of Military Mutual Assistance: Britain Responds to Italian Protests; Prepares to Fulfill Obligations Under the League of Nations Covenant 51

London: Italy protested to Britain on January 24, accusing Britain of adopting extraordinary and unfair plans without first consulting the League of Nations, saying that the secret understanding of a military nature arising from the British memorandum had created an atmosphere of panic that endangered European peace. It should be known that Italy's actions in East Africa are purely of a territorial and colonial nature and will never endanger European peace. Today, the British government has delivered a reply to the Italian Ambassador to Britain, Grandmachi, stating that Britain's position has been stated in the memorandum to the League of Nations Adjustment Committee and does not need to be repeated. It is noted that the British memorandum to the League of Nations detailed the results of the exchange of views between Britain and other governments regarding the situation in the Mediterranean, and in addition to declaring an agreement on mutual assistance between Britain and France in the event of an attack, it also stated that Britain had received assurances from Greece, Turkey, Spain, Yugoslavia, and other countries that they were prepared to faithfully fulfill various obligations under the League of Nations Covenant. (Reuters dispatch, 17th)

U.S. Assistant Secretary of the Navy: To Submit Budget Soon; The Amount Will Be the Largest in Twenty-Five Years 54

France's Loan from Britain: Totaling £60 Million 55

Paris: Regarding the French Ministry of Finance's loan from Britain, the Echo de Paris reported that the loan will be provided by major banks in London. These banks have formed a syndicate, and once British Chancellor of the Exchequer Chamberlain returns to London this morning, it can be formally approved. If there are no unexpected complications, it should be completed by the middle of this week at the latest. "The total loan amount is £60 million in British gold, which is the largest international loan completed in the London market since the war. The annual interest rate is about 3%, and the term is nine months or one year, but the French Ministry of Finance may repay it in advance every three months if it wishes. According to absolutely reliable sources, this loan is only provided by the National Bank Syndicate for the use of the French Treasury, and is not the issuance of treasury bonds by France in the London market for circulation. This proves the strength and stability of the London capital market. As for the rumors that France will make concessions in economic and political aspects as exchange conditions for borrowing from Britain, and that British bankers have requested the Bank of France to provide guarantees, these are not true. We can see from the imminent completion of this loan that France's credit is well-known and trusted by the British financial community. As for France's borrowing of this huge amount, the domestic financial market will be reactivated in the next few weeks, and the currency and bond market conditions will also improve, which is what we can expect." (Havas dispatch, 17th)

Many people watched from the streets, cheering as the parade passed. (Reuters dispatch, 16th)

Economic Discussions 80

— Edited by Tang Qingzeng

The Problem of Risk 81

— Zhao Ren

Risk is the chance of loss or harm. If loss or harm can be predicted to certainly occur, we can take precautions beforehand, estimate the value of the loss or harm, or resign ourselves to fate and let it take its course. If loss or harm is not certain to occur, but there is a possibility of it occurring, and the extent of the loss or harm after it occurs cannot be predicted, then the occurrence and the consequences after the occurrence are all subject to chance. The characteristic of chance is uncertainty, so the origin of risk is also due to uncertainty. It is inevitable that people will grow old and die, but at what age they will die, and how they will die, are all unknowable. For people over ninety-five years old, their lives are truly like morning dew, and they can die at any time. For people in their thirties and forties, who can predict that they will certainly die, and who can predict that they will certainly die prematurely? However, there are indeed people in their thirties and forties who do not die, and there are indeed people in their thirties and forties who die prematurely. Therefore, people in their thirties and forties, although they do not need to worry about their death day and night, cannot be certain that they will not die. The same is true for people of other ages. This is what is called risk. The essence of risk here is survival or death, and the origin of risk here is due to the uncertainty of survival or death. The boiler in a factory will inevitably become old and dilapidated and unable to work after being used for a long time. Therefore, the manager of the factory must estimate the extent of the loss based on the number of years the boiler has been used, and treat it as part of the factory's manufacturing cost. However, some boilers can continue to be used until they are old and dilapidated and unable to work, while others can suddenly explode and be destroyed before the end of their usable life. No one dares to predict which factory's boiler will inevitably explode halfway, but it is possible for every boiler to explode or not to explode. Therefore, all factories equipped with boilers have the risk of boiler explosion, and the origin of risk here is due to the uncertainty of exploding or not exploding. Furthermore, in the operation of a business, the key lies in buying goods at low prices and selling them at high prices to make a profit. However, except for a few who enjoy patent rights or have successfully implemented monopoly policies, the prices of goods going in and out are affected by market supply and demand at any time and place, and fluctuate constantly. If the purchase price is low and the selling price is high, the chance of making a profit is great. If the purchase price is high and the selling price is low, a loss is inevitable. Moreover, the chance of making a profit depends not only on the keen and accurate observation of market changes by the business operator to determine the price and quantity of sales, but also on whether the arrangement of personnel and the raising of funds are appropriate, which can also affect whether or not a profit is made. Proper management can maintain existing capital and even earn a profit, while improper management can lead to losses exceeding capital. Therefore, once a business operator decides on a certain industry, they immediately risk capital loss, and the origin of risk here is due to the uncertainty of using capital to seek profit. As for purchasing real estate and worrying about fire, shipping goods and worrying about sinking, investing in industry and worrying about company bankruptcy, and buying bonds and worrying about the lack of principal and interest, entrepreneurs have the worry of losing capital, and the labor sector feels the suffering of unemployment and idleness. The reason for this is all due to uncertainty. Therefore, the problem of risk is always present in the organization and operation of our social economy.

Risk can be divided into two types: static and dynamic. An individual lives and works in peace and dies or does not die at a certain age, and a house remains or is burned or not burned, are static risks. Racing horses and dying prematurely or not dying, running a business and coping with a volatile market, or losing capital or maintaining capital and having a surplus, are dynamic risks. Risk can also be divided into two types: speculative and pure. Speculative risk has the chance of loss, but also the hope of profit. For example, buying and selling securities and operating industry, commerce, agriculture, and mining. If one is unfortunate and loses, of course there is no way to recover, but if one is fortunate and succeeds, the profit will certainly far exceed expectations. Pure risk, such as houses and machines, if they are burned, the loss can absolutely not be recovered. Even if they are fortunately preserved, they will definitely not increase the hope of profit in addition to the original use efficiency. According to its nature, risk can be divided into five types. The first is natural risk, such as droughts, floods, winds, hailstorms, frosts, snow, and fires. It has a huge impact on harvests, animal husbandry, and transportation, and the arrival of disasters and their consequences are difficult to predict. The second is production risk. Modern production requires machinery and labor. Machines, such as boilers, have the risk of explosion, the cause of which is due to the unsoundness of the materials and the negligence of the managers. The impact of this is to stop production. As for labor, it is difficult to standardize and consistently maintain the efficiency of work, so production cannot be predicted as expected. Moreover, the above-mentioned natural risks are sufficient to cause drastic changes in the source and price of raw materials, causing the result of production, whether in quantity or value, to be reduced at any time. Furthermore, agricultural production relies heavily on the forces of nature, so speculation is most evident. The third is social risk, such as wars, riots, strikes, factory shutdowns, robberies, and counterfeiting. The fourth is the risk of personal ignorance. This risk is due to the individual's failure to take advantage of existing opportunities and knowledge, allowing the keen to compete for and obtain unexpected benefits, while the foolish and weak fall behind and suffer the losses of competition. This is a common phenomenon in commerce, where the pioneers of new businesses advance bravely to make profits, while the followers struggle to keep up. The fifth is market risk. Because there is a time sequence, the supply and demand prices on the market are constantly changing, and merchants have to bear the risk of market price fluctuations caused by time.

Furthermore, there are degrees of risk. If a loss is certain to occur, and even the time of occurrence can be predicted, then no matter how great the loss is, it cannot be called risk. As mentioned earlier, this type of loss can either be left to nature, or precautions can be taken beforehand, or it can be transformed into cost. The greatest risk lies in the point of greatest uncertainty, which is when the probability of success and failure is equal to each other, as in probability logic or mathematics. The further the chance of failure is from the chance of success, the higher the probability of failure, and the smaller its uncertainty or risk. Those who run businesses are actually weighing the gains and losses of their transactions day and night. If a profit can be guaranteed, they will naturally go for it. If a loss is certain, they will either try their best to avoid it, or transform it into cost and incorporate it into the selling price. What they are most uneasy about and cannot resolve is when the gains and losses are close to each other. This is because it is the most uncertain. The common saying "It may make money, it may not make money" expresses this kind of psychology and risk.

The degree of risk varies, and the estimation of risk also varies depending on the person and their circumstances. The middle class, in addition to being able to guarantee food and clothing, has limited financial resources, so even a small loss involves a great sacrifice, and their estimation of various risks must be high. The wealthy have millions of assets, so even a loss of several thousand is not a problem, and their estimation of the same risk must be low. For example, in today's securities market speculation, although both the poor and the rich participate, those with weak financial resources, except for a very few who are willing to make a desperate gamble, are generally satisfied with a small gain. Those with strong financial resources must endure losses to wait for a good price. Since their stakes are large, their expectations must be high, and their losses or profits must be huge. However, this does not mean that those with strong financial resources will not fail. In fact, there are many cases where those with abundant resources have lost repeatedly until they have lost their entire fortunes. However, after all, those with abundant financial resources have a lower estimation of the risk of loss, so they dare to continue speculating. If they lose, they will lose a lot. If they win, they will win a lot. There is also a certain kind of risk for which there is an accurate numerical value that can be verified. For example, tossing a coin and betting that it will land on heads can win ten yuan, but the probability of the coin landing on heads is one-half, and the probability of it landing on tails is also one-half. Multiplying ten yuan by one-half yields five yuan, which is the estimated value of this risk. The operation of life insurance is based on this principle.

Since risk is a universal phenomenon, how should we deal with it? There are three ways: first, to eliminate risk; second, to directly bear the risk oneself; and third, to transfer the risk to others. The first type is like us preparing umbrellas to prevent rain and snow, and building high walls to isolate neighboring fires. In commerce, it is about having detailed and timely statistics on the market, analyzing its supply and demand conditions at any time, and implementing scientific management internally to improve efficiency and eliminate waste. As for human life and death, although it cannot be predicted, it can be shared among many people by life insurance companies, sharing the losses of death. To prevent deposit runs, banks must set aside a sufficient reserve. Importers and exporters simultaneously purchase foreign exchange in the near term and sell it in the far term to avoid exchange rate risk. The second type is like entrepreneurs paying workers a stipulated wage, creditors paying a stipulated interest, and then bearing all other profits and losses themselves. Scholars and playboys mistakenly believe that running a business is like a blind man riding a blind horse, extremely dangerous, but merchants treat it as normal with habit and experience. Although there is a risk of loss, most of them consider it natural and move forward bravely. There are also many capitalists and speculators who directly invest in industry or buy and sell securities themselves. There are a few instances where workers do not ask about the amount of wages, but work directly, seeking income through work opportunities, but the waiters in maritime hotels and restaurants are quite similar to this. The third type is that households with a little savings often entrust banks to invest on their behalf, or deposit money in banks and money shops to earn interest, because they believe that these organizations are better able to bear risk based on their specialized knowledge and experience. Rather than investing directly and having uncertain profits and losses, why not transfer this risk to experts? It is true that banks and money shops are not absolutely safe, but under normal circumstances, their ability to identify investments is stronger than that of private individuals, which cannot be denied. In short, the more complex the social organization and the more developed the credit economy, the more types of risk there are, and the more advanced the methods of preventing risk are due to government supervision and the research of private organizations.

Page 9

Records of Life in the Desert and Wilderness (5) 82

— Jin Dui

(D) Uses and Sales of Livestock: The primary food source for the local Hui and Tibetan people in Gansu Province has traditionally been dairy products. Therefore, mutton in Gansu can almost be considered a staple food. The remaining wool and hides are exported to other provinces as raw materials for weaving. The quantity is also significant. Since the opening of maritime trade after the late Qing Dynasty, they have often been exported to overseas markets. Foreign firms in Shanghai, Tianjin, Hankou, and other places often stationed people in Lintan, Minxian, Xiahe, Jingyuan, Haiyuan, and other counties to purchase locally. Due to the obstructed transportation in the Northwest, the strength of livestock is heavily relied upon for transportation. Consequently, cattle, horses, donkeys, mules, and camels have all become essential means of transportation. Among cattle, the large flat cattle produced in Minxian are valued for their strength and docility, making them ideal for driving carts and plowing fields. The small hairy cattle, also known as zebu cattle, produced in Xiahe, Liancheng, and other places are mostly used for labor and are transported to various parts of the provincial capital for their milk and meat for human consumption. The horses from Yongdeng, Lintan, and Minxian are sold annually to Henan, Shaanxi, and other provinces as military horses, in considerable numbers.

7. The Wool Industry in Gansu

Gansu borders Shaanxi, Suiyuan, Ningxia, Qinghai, and other provinces. Its climate is roughly the same as that of the northwestern provinces. Due to the favorable local conditions, animal husbandry is most suitable, as mentioned in the previous article. Consequently, a majority of the people make a living by nomadism, with sheep herding being the most prevalent, unlike the southeastern provinces where sheep raising is considered a sideline. The wool produced annually, apart from supplying the province for the manufacture of woolen blankets, coarse wool fabrics, rugs, and various knitted woolen goods, is exported every year. According to the Gansu Republic Daily, a survey conducted in 1932 (Year 21 of the Republic) found that spring wool production was 15,406 dan (each dan weighing 100 jin), priced at 20 yuan per dan, totaling 308,120 yuan. Autumn wool production was 15,406 dan, priced at 25 yuan per dan, totaling 385,150 yuan. A survey in 1933 (Year 22 of the Republic) found that spring wool production was 21,362 dan, priced at 20 yuan per dan, totaling 427,240 yuan. Autumn wool production was 21,362 dan, priced at 25 yuan per dan, totaling 534,050 yuan. According to statistics from the Department of Construction, a survey in 1934 (Year 23 of the Republic), based solely on detailed reports from 28 counties, showed a total annual production of 1,329,438 kilograms, with an annual value of 618,949 yuan. If a comprehensive calculation were to be made for all counties throughout the year, the figure would undoubtedly be even higher. The abundant wool production is evident.

Wool is generally divided into two types: cotton sheep wool (white sheep wool) and goat wool (black sheep wool). In addition to these two types, Gansu also produces what is called wool, which comes from a goat with long white hair. It can be used to make leather clothing and felt blankets and woolen fabrics but is not suitable for making woolen cloth because it has too little fine down and is too stiff. Another type is called purple sheep wool, which comes from a cotton sheep with long black hair. It is mostly produced in Tibet, hence its other name, Tibetan sheep. It is best for making leather clothing because it has more fine down and strong heat-retention properties, making it suitable for keeping warm even in the severe winter. Moreover, black wool from cotton sheep is quite rare, making it very popular.

For wool used in textile raw materials, the preference is for fibers that are fine, long, and have considerable elasticity and luster. They can be woven into various woolen fabrics and dyed in any color. Moreover, the natural yield of this type is relatively abundant among all types of wool. Wool that possesses these characteristics is cotton sheep wool. Conversely, fibers that are uneven in thickness, dull in color, and cannot be dyed to satisfaction, with cotton sheep yielding only one jin of wool per shearing compared to the half jin yielded by goats, are the disadvantages of goat wool.

Shearing wool is largely done in two seasons: spring and autumn. The spring shearing period is around the Qingming Festival. The wool has endured severe cold weather in the winter and contains the most down and the finest fibers. Wool sheared at this time is called spring wool. The autumn shearing period is around the Mid-Autumn Festival. The wool has been exposed to hot weather in the summer and contains a high oil content and stronger elasticity. Wool sheared at this time is called autumn wool. In addition, there is plucked wool and sheep down, mostly plucked in the summer. As for pelt wool, it is the waste wool scraped off during the manufacture of leather clothing and leather, also called dead wool, containing a high amount of lime and cannot be dyed.

During the spring and autumn seasons, when wool comes to market, wool merchants purchase it in the pastoral areas and transport it to the cities, reselling it to woolen manufacturers. Due to the remote location and inconvenient transportation, direct purchasing from inland areas to Gansu has been rare in recent years. In the areas inhabited by the Tibetans and other ethnic minorities, wool is still exchanged for daily necessities. This seems to be a remnant of the "barter" system from thousands of years ago, which they still retain. As for ordinary wool trade, there are no standard weights and measures. Some scales use sixteen or twenty-four taels as one jin, while others use thirty-two taels as one jin. These variations are likely due to the vast distances, complex ethnicities, and different customs. In recent years, the domestic and international economic downturn has affected the wool sales, which have plummeted. Gansu has traditionally relied on wool as a major export commodity. If improvements can be made and the wool industry revitalized, it would benefit China, promote domestic goods, recover foreign earnings, and contribute to the development of the Northwest.

Massive Fire in Nanshi, Tianjin 83

Warming Shelter Burns Down, 150 Killed: Charred Bones and Corpses Litter the Ground, a Horrific Sight

Tianjin Dispatch: The warming shelter run by the Mingde Charity Association and the porridge kitchen run by the Chinese Merchants Association behind the Grand Theater in Qinghe Street, Tianjin's Nanshi District, caught fire unexpectedly at 2:50 AM yesterday (the 14th) and were completely destroyed. A total of 149 men and women perished in the inferno, making it an unprecedented tragedy. The details are as follows:

Facilities of the Warming Shelter

The Mingde Charity Association in the Japanese Concession of this city is organized by a group of gentry and merchants. Last year, to shelter the homeless from the severe cold, they established a warming shelter in October on the vacant land behind the Grand Theater in Nanshi, a place where the lower strata of Tianjin society gather. It was quite popular. In December, they expanded part of it, accommodating up to 300 or 400 homeless people. At the time of the fire, there were about 200 people staying there. Adjacent to the north of the warming shelter was the porridge kitchen established by the Chinese Merchants Association. The two groups cooperated, with the Chinese Merchants Association providing porridge at noon and the warming shelter providing food in the evening. In total, more than 1,000 people ate there daily. The two places occupied a vast area of 20 mu. The warming shelter was constructed with bamboo poles and reed mats, a total of four layers, to prevent wind penetration. The ground was covered with straw and multiple layers of waste newspaper. In addition to the boiler, there were also several large coal stoves inside. The homeless considered it a blessed place and flocked to the shelter. Men and women were separated into two sections. Even during the severe cold, it was very comfortable. Even rickshaw pullers and peddlers abandoned their homes to stay there.

Sudden Fire

The warming shelter had two managers and five watchmen who patrolled at night. However, with so many people accommodated, there was a mix of good and bad. The front and back doors were locked at night. The Sixth Precinct of the First Public Security Bureau, which was in charge of the area, also sent officers to inspect from time to time. Unexpectedly, at 2:50 AM yesterday, when all was quiet, a fire suddenly broke out. The internal structure of the warming shelter was highly flammable. In an instant, flames soared, illuminating several miles around. The nearby patrol police discovered it and immediately reported it to the Public Security Bureau. All eight fire brigades in the city were dispatched. However, because the fire had already engulfed the entire shelter, the water hoses could do little. So they focused on rescuing people. At that time, screams filled the air, a most tragic scene. It was not until 5:30 AM that the fire was completely extinguished.

Number of Deaths

Apart from those who escaped, the number of deaths, after investigation, was 149, including 141 men (including one watchman), 6 women, and 3 children (2 boys and 1 girl). The corpses were exposed on the spot. The Tianjin District Court sent prosecutors to examine them at 3:00 PM. In the evening, the Public Welfare Society prepared coffins and buried all the bodies. The Director of the Public Security Bureau, Liu Yushu, visited the scene at 10:00 AM. In the evening, he invited monks to pray for the dead. When reporters visited the scene, many spectators were present. The corpses were piled up to one side, completely charred. Some had their internal organs exposed. The scene was so tragic that it was unbearable to witness.

Relief Measures

The cause of the fire has not yet been determined. The Sixth Precinct of the First District has taken the four watchmen, Wang Jialin, Li Wengui (from the Mingde Charity Association warming shelter), Pang Zixi, and Cao Zhenlin (from the Chinese Merchants Association porridge kitchen), to the Public Security Bureau for interrogation. Their statements did not reveal the cause of the fire. The City Public Security Bureau has ordered the staff of the Mingde Charity Association to report the truth and has also sent people to investigate everything in order to handle the aftermath and relief work. The Mingde Charity Association held an emergency meeting at 3:00 PM on the 15th to discuss the handling of the aftermath. They resolved to ask the Public Welfare Society for materials and to provide compensation to the families of the deceased. The meeting adjourned at 5:00 PM. The compensation plan has also been drafted and will be implemented immediately.

Attitude of the Authorities

After receiving the report, the Tianjin Municipal Government sent Inspector Tian Jiuying to conduct an on-site investigation and handle the matter. It is reported that the Chairman of the Mingde Charity Association, Zhong Shiming, considered himself responsible for the matter and avoided meeting with anyone yesterday. Currently, Zhao Pinqing, Chairman of the Charity Federation, Xiao Shaotang, Director of the Public Welfare Society, and Liu Daopeng, Chairman of the Red Cross Society, are separately responsible for handling the aftermath. The unclaimed bodies have been temporarily buried in the public cemetery in Wangjiazhuang in the western suburbs.

Hebei-Chahar Negotiations: Still Many Thorns Ahead 84

Yin Rugeng Demands that Eastern Hebei Be Changed to a Special Administrative Region; The Administration of the Six Counties in Northern Chahar Has Not Yet Been Restored to Its Original State

Beiping Dispatch: The Hebei-Chahar diplomatic issue has made little progress due to the excessive demands. The issue of abolishing the organization in Eastern Hebei is not even being discussed at this moment. Yin Rugeng has two demands: (1) that Eastern Hebei be changed to a special administrative region with Yin as the chief administrator; and (2) that the five provinces of North China be autonomous. The Beiping authorities have not approved these demands. Therefore, diplomatic negotiations are not easy to conduct at this time. Song Zheyuan, Chairman of the Hebei-Chahar Political Affairs Committee, received Xiao Zhenying, Qin Dechun, and Feng Zhi'an at his private residence this morning (the 16th) and inquired about important matters. According to Tianjin Mayor Xiao Zhenying, the Hebei-Chahar diplomacy is currently under separate negotiation. The Economic Committee held a meeting yesterday to discuss the financial reorganization of the two provinces of Hebei and Chahar and the two cities of Beiping and Tianjin. Whether Wang Tianyou's case will be settled in Beiping is still uncertain. I am scheduled to return to Tianjin tomorrow to handle political affairs.

After Luo Jiaheng, the Chahar Diplomatic Commissioner, arrived in Beiping, he discussed the Chahar issue with Chen Zhongfu, Chairman of the Foreign Affairs Committee. Tonight, Luo will return to Shanghai via Beijing and will first report the recent situation of Chahar's diplomacy to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs before going to Shanghai. He is expected to return to the north in two weeks. According to Luo, I arrived in Tianjin at the end of last month and went to Zhangjiakou on the 6th of this month. At that time, rumors were rampant, but the facts are not so. The authorities are very firm in their intention not to give up land lightly. Li Shouxin and Zhuo Shihai's troops, totaling more than 2,000, are divided into independent teams and security teams and have no intention of moving south. The year number on their proclamations is the number of years since Genghis Khan. The administration of the six counties in northern Chahar has not been restored to its original state because negotiations have not yet been completed.

Doihara, the representative of the Japanese Kwantung Army, recently made a statement, saying that everything has progressed since the establishment of the Hebei-Chahar Political Affairs Committee. The Eastern Hebei region has some misunderstandings with the committee. Once the misunderstandings are cleared up, the two sides can be expected to unite. Regarding the Hebei-Chahar Political Affairs Committee hiring consultants, if the committee wishes to hire Japanese technicians, I am very willing to introduce them. My current task in staying in Beiping is to strive for peace between China and Japan. All issues are being discussed in turn. Li Shouxin in northern Chahar has a close relationship with the Mongolian side, but not with Manchukuo. It is said that they have no intention of advancing towards the Sui border. As for De Wang, he travels back and forth constantly due to the geographical relationship between Mongolia and Manchuria, but he has not discussed any other issues except seeking local stability.

The internal organization of the Hebei-Chahar Diplomatic Committee is divided into two groups: General Affairs and Political Affairs. Each group is divided into three sections, with four secretaries and three to five specialists. The heads of each section have already been announced. The head of the first section of the General Affairs Group is Lin Gengyu, the head of the second section is Xu Wenyuan (acting as a first-class staff member), and the head of the third section is Ou Daqing. Hu Zheng and Ou Xiaoqing have been announced as secretaries. Four specialists have been internally appointed and will be announced in the next few days. The committee has appointed three additional members: Tang Yueliang, Ren Yuandao, and Zhang Yuquan. Tang has arrived in Beiping, while Zhang and Ren are still staying in Shanghai (16th).

Tianjin Exempts Burdensome Taxes 85

Merchants and Citizens Gain Opportunity for Resuscitation; City Government Compensates for Municipal Taxes by Sealing Off the Huili Ball Field

Tianjin Dispatch: Since Xiao Zhenying became the mayor of Tianjin, he has shown a strong intention to let the people rest and recuperate. Shortly after taking office, he first exempted eight types of burdensome taxes in Tianjin. As a member of the Hebei-Chahar Political Affairs Committee, he suggested to Song Zheyuan that three types of water transport taxes on ships in the five rivers of Hebei Province be exempted. For a time, merchants and citizens celebrated. Recently, four other types of taxes, including stall taxes, reed mat taxes, and entertainment taxes, are being reviewed and will soon be abolished. In recent years, Tianjin's commerce has been troubled by both internal and external factors. Internally, the market is sluggish, the rural economy is bankrupt, and the purchasing power of urban and rural areas is weak, causing all industries to stagnate. Externally, Japanese and Korean ruffians smuggle goods with evaded tariffs, which are then sold by unscrupulous merchants, affecting legitimate businessmen. Furthermore, the heavy and complicated taxes have put merchants in a state of moaning and struggling to survive. The city government's decision to exempt and reduce taxes has given hope to the general business community. Since the Spring Festival, various industries in the city have been slightly active. Although it has not yet reached a great situation, if the market remains calm as it is now, a turning point can be expected in the second half of the year. Xiao Zhenying is determined to revive the Chinese area and has instructed Ji Hua, chairman of the Chamber of Commerce, to draft a plan. If it is permitted by the regulations, he will resolve to implement it to relieve the general suffering. Therefore, Ji Hua is currently reviewing and drafting a plan. The City Chamber of Commerce, the Money Industry Association, and other organizations are planning to hold a "Huanghui" fair in mid-March of the lunar calendar to revitalize the market. The so-called "Huanghui" is a type of northern fair that brings together people from the city and countryside to a market for several days of processions. During these days, all kinds of arts and crafts are displayed, and the gold industry also celebrates with lanterns. The government waives all import and export and local taxes during this period. Fifteen years ago, Tianjin used to hold it in early spring. On the day of the fair, the streets were deserted, and many villagers came to the city to visit. According to the Chamber of Commerce, this is not to promote superstition but to use this event to create a buzz and attract people from all directions. All industries can display their goods during the fair for people to see and learn about the product. This is like the wheat festival celebrations in the West or an exhibition. Tianjin merchants have been like fish trapped in a dry rut for a long time. If they can get tax exemptions during the fair, they can take the opportunity to import some goods. The government loses very little, but the merchants benefit greatly. The city government has already agreed to this. However, Tianjin's tax revenue last year was already strained due to the rapid changes in the political situation, frequent personnel changes, and the fatigue of commerce and industry. The city's budget requires more than 5 million yuan per year, and with the various contributions, it requires more than 7 million yuan per year. If the previous year's example is followed this year, tax revenue will be at most 5 or 6 million yuan. Exempting various miscellaneous taxes totals more than 300,000 yuan. Although the amount is not huge, at this time, losing one cent is like missing ten thousand. Therefore, the city government is trying its best to find ways to compensate. However, compensating cannot mean adding burdens to the citizens. Therefore, they thought of the Italian-owned Huili Ball Field, ordering it to pay 100,000 yuan in charity donations annually. According to the authorities, although the Huili Ball Field is located in the Italian concession, 90% of the gamblers are Chinese. Since its establishment, countless men and women who gamble have lost their fortunes and even committed suicide by drowning or poisoning. Since the victims are all Chinese, the Chinese government has no way to ban it, so it can only order it to pay a sum of charity money to be used for the city's construction, to atone for its sins and prevent citizens from resenting it too much. Last month, Xiao Zhenying ordered Liu Dongxuan, director of the Social Affairs Bureau, to negotiate. The Italian directors of the Huili Ball Field took a tough stance and refused to accept the intention. The city government then issued a warning, saying that if they did not comply, they would order the Second and Third Special Districts to seal off the Italian Concession. Because the Italian Concession is located in Hebei and is between the Second and Third Special Districts, gamblers must pass through the two districts every night. Italy initially did not budge but then agreed to pay 20,000 yuan annually, which the city government did not accept. The two sides reached a stalemate. Since the 13th of this month, the Public Security Bureaus of the Second and Third Special Districts have secretly ordered all public transportation companies and rental cars not to pick up or drop off gamblers at the Huili Ball Field. Those who are found will be severely punished. Private individuals who go to gamble are secretly investigated and warned. Even rickshaws are restricted. Therefore, in recent days, the Huili Ball Field has been unusually deserted, and even the dance floor is dimly lit and sparsely populated. However, the Italian concession authorities still maintain their tough stance and refuse to yield, so the stalemate continues (15th).

Britain Hastens Construction of Singapore Naval Base 86

Chaoshan Workers Flock South to Work

Shantou Dispatch: After the London Disarmament Conference, Britain decided to allocate an additional 300 million pounds to strengthen its national defense and protect British interests in the world and the Far East, open an air route from Menam (transliteration) to Hong Kong, send airships to visit Japan, and build up Hong Kong's naval and air bases. Because Britain's seven-year military buildup plan is now nearing completion, all projects are being rushed, costing a total of 30,000,000 pounds. Singapore has become the world's largest naval base and the only fortress to protect interests in the Far East. Seven years ago, a large floating dock, 855 feet long and 178 feet wide, was completed in that year. It can accommodate giant ships of 50,000 tons, dragging them out of the water. The floating dock can accommodate 60,000 people standing on it. When it was towed from Wallsend to Singapore, it required eight tugboats and took three months. The floating dock is called No. 9. Britain has a larger floating dock, No. 8, located in Malta, a naval base in the Mediterranean. Malta's strategic location is important, serving as a backup naval port for the Strait of Gibraltar. Singapore's seven-year plan is undoubtedly related to this location. The No. 9 dock is located in Seletar, Singapore, covering an area of 2,800 acres, more than four square miles, and is the most modern and complete naval and air base. In addition, there is a 600-acre naval and air aviation landing field. The land was originally a desolate, uninhabited forest but has now been transformed into steel-roofed aircraft hangars, repair shops, barracks, and other complete facilities. At the southern end of the airfield is the largest radio station, which can be used for military communications between London, Hong Kong, and Shanghai. The village of Changzhao, Singapore, has been transformed into barracks for infantry, artillery, and engineers. Solid fortifications have been built on the mountains near the engineers' barracks, with anti-aircraft guns and long-range artillery. Chinese workers have contributed greatly to the construction of this massive project. Singapore has become the world's seventh-largest port and a major transportation route between the East and West Oceans and a prosperous commercial route. It now has a population of 440,000, with whites (excluding soldiers) accounting for 7,600. It is Britain's most productive colony. During the British Imperial Conference in 1912, New Zealand Prime Minister Massey said that if a hypothetical war were to occur with a certain powerful Eastern nation, without the solid naval and air base in Singapore, Australia and New Zealand would be unable to send troops to assist. At the British Imperial Conference in 1922, Britain abolished the Anglo-Japanese Alliance in the Pacific and insisted on establishing a naval base in Singapore, so that the British Far East Fleet would have a place to repair and refuel. In 1924, British important figure Hankey visited Singapore and, after returning home, submitted a memorandum on the importance of establishing a military port in Singapore. Thus, the seven-year plan was established. All countries with interests in the Far East (USA, France, Netherlands) are protected by the Singapore military port, except for Japan, which opposes it.

Jiading: Civil Servants Build Ring Road Around the City 87

Civil servants from various county government agencies have, in compliance with orders, begun three days of labor service starting on the 17th to build the northeastern ring road connecting the Jialuo bus station to the Jialou Road. Each person is responsible for 13.5 cubic meters of earthwork, totaling more than 150 people. The land has been divided and construction has been restricted. Yesterday morning at 9:00 AM, a groundbreaking ceremony was held at the bus station, after which service was put into practice.

Kunshan: Private Opium Smoker Dies of Illness in Prison 88

Huang Kejin, a local villager in his thirties, was arrested by the Qianyan Anti-Smoking Association last August for smoking opium without a license. He was handed over to the judiciary and sentenced to six months in prison, which is about to expire. Suddenly, he suffered a severe fever and chills the other day. Despite various medical treatments, he died in prison on the morning of the 15th. The county government sent personnel to inspect and confirmed that he died of illness. The relief society prepared a coffin and buried him.

Police Officer Assaults and Injures Detained Tenant Farmer 89

Last year, the county detained a large number of tenant farmers who owed rent. Their lives were extremely difficult. The other night, three detained tenant farmers, including Chen, got up to urinate. They searched everywhere for a urinal but could not find one, so they urinated in a corner. A police officer saw this and immediately lashed out with a whip, adding punches and kicks. All three were injured. Tenant farmer Wang Qingtang was the most seriously injured. The next day, he was carried to the Minshang Clinic for examination and treatment. It was found that his lower abdomen was kicked and his life was in danger. The three were later transferred to the county hospital for treatment.

Wuxi: Sixty-Year-Old Man Injured Resisting Robbers 90

Yu Xirong, a resident of Xialang Village, Tangtou Town, Fifth District of the county, has been working as a silk pawnshop clerk at the Yongtai Jiang Transportation Company. His father, A San, is sixty-three years old. Both father and son are strong and powerful. The other night, eight robbers broke into their house to rob them. Yu Xirong and his father were awakened from their dreams. Hastily, they rang the gong to call for help and used door bolts to knock down one robber. Another robber was also pinned down by Yu Xirong and could not move. However, the robbers were too many. Yu Xirong was stabbed in the back by a robber with a broadsword, injuring his lungs. A San was also stabbed. Seeing that they had caused trouble, the robbers snatched two leather suitcases and many clothes, totaling more than three hundred yuan, and fled in a panic. The incident has been reported to the county government through the Public Security Bureau. The injured person was also brought to the city for treatment. It is said that his condition is extremely serious, but his life is not yet in danger.

Expanding Silkworm Breeding Guidance Center 91

Last year, the county's silk industry rebounded, and all silk factories in Xidi made double profits. Therefore, the interest of farmers raising silkworms is also very strong. During the winter last year, they had already placed orders for spring silkworm eggs at the model silkworm farming area's guidance centers. After a thorough investigation by the model area, the county needs 300,000 sheets of spring silkworm eggs this year, which have already been prepared. Currently, 150,000 sheets have already been ordered. However, because the number of silk farmers has increased, the guidance center has decided to expand to 95 locations, an increase of 15 locations compared to last year. Funding has been approved by the Department of Construction. In addition, to facilitate farmers' own drying of cocoons, cocoon stoves of four multipliers and below will be checked and registered.

Changzhou: Stamp Tax Committee Member Goes to Wuxi After Completing Work 92

Li Guoqi, a Stamp Tax Inspector from the Ministry of Finance, and Tong Yixiang, a Supervising Committee member from the Jiangsu Finance Department, supervised the county inspectors Zheng Bin to inspect stamp taxes in the city and countryside in the city and the countryside. All stores were able to deeply understand the importance of national taxes and follow the rules. A mere ten violations of the stamp tax law involving underpayment have been found. On the 16th, Commissioner Li went to Benniu, Commissioner Tong went to Henglin, and Commissioner Zheng went to Qishuyan and other places to investigate separately. No violations were found. Commissioners Li and Tong decided to compile the results of their work and send the few violations to the county on the 17th, which will be forwarded to the county court for punishment. They decided to leave Changzhou for Wuxi on the 18th to work.

Yangzhou, Security Department Captures Bandits in Yangzhou 93

According to confessions from bandits captured by the Zhenjiang Security Command, accomplices were hiding in a thatched shed on Shang Street outside the North Gate of Yangzhou. The command dispatched five service personnel, including Shao Hanzhang, along with informants, arriving in Yangzhou on the 15th. They cooperated with the local county's detective division and the third branch of the public security bureau, sending police to the address, where they captured the bandit Wang Dezhi, his mother Wang Guo, and neighbor Wang Xuetian, a total of three people. They were temporarily detained in the detective team and escorted back to Zhenjiang on the 16th for further investigation.

Hangzhou, Agricultural Extension Conference in Various Counties 94

The Zhejiang Provincial Department of Construction, in order to develop agricultural production and relieve rural areas, has stipulated that agriculture is the central construction focus for this year, with a large-scale promotion of rice, wheat, and cotton covering a total of 300,000 mu. As the sowing season approaches, the local conditions in the designated improvement area counties may vary. The Haining Seawall is Already in a Precarious State 95

The Zhejiang Province coastal seawall stretches for hundreds of miles. Due to years of disrepair, the seawall body is riddled with holes, and the situation is critical. However, the provincial treasury is depleted, and there are no funds available for repairs. As the spring floods are approaching, if proper protection is not provided, a single accident would have significant consequences. Zhou Zhenlun, Director of the Water Conservancy Bureau, took a car yesterday to inspect the Haining section of the seawall along the coast and returned to the province in the evening. According to him, the most dangerous sections of the seawall are those between Haining and the eighth (number missing) section, with the Gongmao and other marked areas being the worst. The seawall body is leaning forward and sloping downwards, making the situation extremely dangerous. Additionally, the Wuduo and other marked areas have been using earthen dikes for defense since the seawall body collapsed last year, which could lead to danger if impacted by tides. There are many other dangerous seawall projects. He has instructed the engineering office of the section to prepare a detailed plan to be submitted to the province to request funds for repairs, in order to avoid accidents.
