Local News

Shanghai Chinese Merchants Securities Exchange: Yesterday, Discussions First, Trading Commenced in the Afternoon 96

Du Yuesheng and Others Met with Kong Xiangxi to Discuss Market Opening Measures; Opening Up of New Purchases Caused All Bonds to Fall; Clearing of February Futures as Usual Today

The Shanghai Chinese Merchants Securities Exchange, in accordance with the order of the Ministry of Finance, announced that it would open the market yesterday morning. However, upon the request of the Brokers Association, the market opened at 4:30 p.m. and only conducted one session. Du Yuesheng, Zhang Weiru, and He Peiyuan met with Kong Xiangxi yesterday to discuss the market opening measures. Yesterday, the prices of all bonds uniformly declined. The details are as follows:

Temporary Announcement to Conduct Only One Session

The Shanghai Chinese Merchants Securities Exchange announced yesterday morning that, after the market opening, upon the request of the Brokers Association, it issued Announcement No. 2255, stating, "We have received a letter from the Brokers Association, stating that member firms have reported that they need to contact clients separately today, and the procedures are complicated and time-consuming. Please forward a letter to the Exchange, allowing for an extension to 4:30 p.m. for trading and changing to one session, etc. This request is hereby approved. All transactions for today will be changed to one session and will be allowed to commence at 4:30 p.m. This is hereby announced."

Meeting with Minister Kong to Discuss Measures

The Brokers Association of the Exchange resolved two remedial measures: 1. Open up new purchases to stabilize market prices; 2. Cancel physical delivery. They immediately dispatched Association Chairman He Peiyuan and others to meet with Exchange Chairman Zhang Weiru to request that it be submitted to the Ministry of Finance for approval. At 12:00 noon yesterday, Du Yuesheng, Zhang Weiru, He Peiyuan, and three others went to the Central Bank to meet with Minister of Finance Kong Xiangxi to report on the resolution of the Brokers Association and to explain the reasons. At that time, Minister Kong opened up new purchases, but physical delivery was still required in accordance with the Ministry's order. They departed at 1:00 p.m.

The Brokers Association Held a General Meeting

The Brokers Association of the Exchange held a general meeting at 1:30 p.m. yesterday on the eighth floor of the Exchange. All brokers sent representatives, and Exchange Chairman Zhang Weiru and Director Du Yuesheng were present. Association Chairman He Peiyuan presided over the meeting and reported on the meeting with Minister of Finance Kong Xiangxi. The approval of opening up new purchases, while still requiring physical delivery, had largely resolved the issue of stabilizing market prices. At that time, everyone unanimously approved opening the market at 4:30 p.m. in accordance with the Ministry's order. The meeting adjourned at 4:00 p.m.

Trading Resumed Yesterday Afternoon

The market opened at 4:30 p.m. yesterday, and all brokers entered the market as usual. For various government bonds and treasury bills, the old names were still used. Only new purchase transactions were allowed, and new sale transactions were not allowed. Only the February futures contracts, which were expiring on the 29th with 63 million yuan of transactions, were traded. Securities that were previously sold short were now allowed to be covered, and bonds that were previously bought were now allowed to be sold, entirely for the purpose of clearing previous accounts. Yesterday, all bonds uniformly declined. Trading will continue as usual today. As for when the Unified National Bonds and Reconstruction Bonds will be traded, it is still awaiting a clear order from the Ministry of Finance.

Bond Prices Uniformly Declined

Yesterday's opening prices: Consolidation Bond opened at 32.8 yuan, closed at 33.5 yuan, previously 35.4 yuan; Disbandment Bond opened at 67.2 yuan, closed at 66.3 yuan, previously 70.5 yuan; 1920 Customs Bond at 30 yuan, previously 33.8 yuan; 1920 Rehabilitation Bond at 34.5 yuan, previously 38.9 yuan; 20th Year Tobacco Tax Bond at 40.1 yuan, previously 44.3 yuan; 20th Year Customs Duty Bond opened at 44.1 yuan, closed at 44.3 yuan, previously 46.26 yuan; Unified Tax Bond at 46 yuan, previously 50.05 yuan; 20th Year Salt Tax Bond at 47 yuan, previously 51.1 yuan; 20th Year Financial Bond at 67 yuan, previously 71.4 yuan; 22nd Year Customs Duty Bond at 53 yuan, previously 56.45 yuan; 23rd Year Customs Duty Bond opened at 52.3 yuan, closed at 52 yuan, previously 56 yuan; Full-Six Bond at 65 yuan, previously 69 yuan; Nine-Six Bond opened at 9 yuan, closed at 9.5 yuan, previously 10.75 yuan. "Previously" refers to the market prices on January 29th.

Commission Losses of 300,000 Yuan

A reporter from the New Voice News Agency learned from the Shanghai Chinese Merchants Securities Exchange last night that the total transaction amount for yesterday afternoon's 4:30 session was over 3.8 million yuan. Since the market was suspended on January 30th by order of the Ministry, based on the January 29th transaction amount of 34.725 million yuan, and calculating a commission of 6.25 yuan per transaction, the Exchange should have earned approximately 20,000 yuan in commissions per day. As of yesterday, the market had been suspended for 18 days, including two Sundays and 16 working days, resulting in a total estimated loss of 300,000 yuan.

Various Banks Actively Accept Bonds as Collateral

The Ministry of Finance had previously ordered the Bank of China, the Central Bank, and the Bank of Communications to calculate the Unified National Bonds used as issuance and savings guarantee reserves at 70% of the face value. It is said that the Ministry of Finance has agreed to instruct the Bank of China, the Central Bank, and the Bank of Communications to accept all classes of Unified National Bonds as collateral, in order to encourage the public to purchase government bonds. At the same time, the Ministry will allocate funds to establish a price stabilization committee to stabilize bond prices.

New Government Bonds Temporarily Unavailable for Trading

According to Shenshi News, in addition to the 25th Year Unified National Bonds, the Exchange will also trade several other types of government bonds, including the 17th Year Financial Long-Term Bonds, the 17th Year Rehabilitation Short-Term Bonds, and the Short-Term Bonds for Dredging the Hai River Project in Hebei Province. As for the Reconstruction Bonds, since they have not yet been issued, they cannot be traded at the same time. Regarding the method for exchanging old bonds for new Unified National Bonds, the Ministry of Finance will announce it soon. It is said that the new Unified National Bonds will not be fully printed until April 20th. The various bonds will be exchanged in stages starting from the 31st of this month, with the exchange expected to be completed by the end of June this year. Holders of old bonds can request exchange from the local Bank of China, Central Bank, or Bank of Communications within the legal period. The three banks will collect and send them to the Shanghai Bond Exchange Center for exchange and distribution. Before the exchange, old bonds specified in the Unified National Bonds will be regarded as having the same effect as certain bonds. In addition, there is also the Reconstruction Bond, the new notes of which have been printed at the same time as the Unified National Bond, but the date of full printing will be after April 21st. The Ministry of Finance has already printed the subscription vouchers for the Reconstruction Bond, which will be issued soon. However, the underwriting issue of these bonds has not yet been decided.

Lottery Dates for Unified National and Reconstruction Bonds

The Ministry of Finance has stipulated the lottery dates for the Unified National and Reconstruction Bonds as follows: (First Drawing) Unified National Bonds Class A and B, May 10th of this year; Unified National Bonds Class C and D, June 10th of this year; Unified National Bonds Class E, July 10th of this year; Reconstruction Bonds, July 10th of this year; (Second Drawing) Unified National Bonds Class A, August and February 10th each year; Unified National Bonds Class B, September and March 10th each year; Unified National Bonds Class C, October and April 10th each year; Unified National Bonds Class D, November and May 10th each year; Unified National Bonds Class E, December and June 10th each year; Reconstruction Bonds, January and July 10th each year.

Government Bond Discount Activities Facilitate Finance

A reporter from the Guowen News Agency learned from the National Debt Fund Management Committee yesterday that the committee has agreed with the Bank of China, the Central Bank, and the Bank of Communications to discount unmatured principal and interest coupons and unredeemed interest coupons using the principal and interest repayment funds deposited in the three banks. The repayment of principal and interest for various types of Unified National Bonds is set for January and July. The repayment of principal and interest for the Reconstruction Bonds is set for February and August. The redemption dates for the drawings have been advanced, and drawings will be held monthly throughout the year. Bondholders can also request discounts from banks. Once a bond is drawn, the redeemed bond and all current interest coupons, even if not yet due, are no different from cash, which greatly facilitates financial activities.

This City, Unprecedented Heavy Fog Yesterday Morning 97

Difficult to Distinguish Objects Beyond Two Feet, Land, Sea, and Air Transportation All Obstructed

The weather in this city has been warm these past days, with a hint of the New Year spirit. However, heavy fog is commonly seen every morning. A heavy fog suddenly appeared around 10:00 p.m. the night before last, and it did not gradually dissipate until 10:00 a.m. yesterday. Land, sea, and air transportation were all obstructed for a time. The details of each situation are as follows:

Cars Moving Slowly

The fog began at 10:00 p.m. the night before last and was heaviest around 5:00 a.m. yesterday. It was almost impossible to distinguish people and objects beyond two feet. Therefore, cars on the road did not dare to drive fast, and only crept along slowly. At the same time, trams turned on their red lights and also moved slowly to prevent accidents. Pedestrians on the road were all cautious, because beyond two steps, they could only hear the sound of car horns and could not see the body of the car.

Ships Obstructed

The fog obstructed all ships entering and leaving the port. According to inquiries at the Customs' ship entry and exit office, the Changhai ships that were scheduled to leave the port around 8:00 a.m. yesterday, including the Jardine Matheson's Jihe, the Sanbei's Fengpu, the China Merchants' Jiangshun, and the Taikoo's Changsha, were all delayed until after 12:00 p.m. before they reluctantly left the port. In addition, the Shanghai-Ningbo lines New Beijing, New Ningbo-Shaoxing, and New Hongxing were also delayed until the afternoon before leaving the port. There were also more than a dozen ships blocked outside the port, all of which began to slowly enter the Wusongkou after 12:00 p.m. As for civilian ships, the Suzhou River area was also impassable due to the extremely heavy fog. Those that did depart around 11:00 a.m. moved very slowly and their steam whistles sounded continuously.

Shops Lit Lamps

As for airplanes, since the Eurasia Company did not have any flights scheduled on its various routes yesterday, there were no airplanes flying out. The China National Aviation Corporation's Shanghai-Guangzhou line also did not have any flights scheduled yesterday. Only the Shanghai-Hankou-Xi'an plane was blocked and delayed until around 1:00 p.m. before it was able to take off. Also, during the foggy hours, many shops on the main streets lit lamps to welcome customers.

Rent Reduction Committee Submits Another Petition to the Executive Yuan, Elucidating the Reasons for Requesting Rent Reduction 99

And Requests Heavy Land Value Tax and Vacant House Tax to Be Levied to Suppress Rent Gouging and Seek Market Prosperity

The Shanghai Rent Reduction Committee, in response to news reports that the Executive Yuan was convening relevant departments to hold a meeting to discuss solutions for Shanghai's rent reduction issue, submitted a petition to the Executive Yuan yesterday, elucidating the reasons for requesting a clear order for a 60% rent reduction. The original text read (omitted above). The reasons for requesting rent reduction are presented to your Yuan as follows: "Request for a 60% rent reduction: The real estate industry earns revenue from rent, similar to earning interest on savings. If someone deposits 1,000 yuan, they can earn 10 yuan in interest per month. The standard for rent determination is based on the combined cost of land price and construction cost, so rent levels vary, but the interest rates are similar. Unifying the rent reduction to 60% is equivalent to reducing interest by 60%. Furthermore, Article 442 of the Civil Code states, 'If the leased object is immovable property, the parties may petition the court to increase or decrease the rent due to the rise or fall in its value.' According to legal provisions, rent reduction is a legal act. Moreover, the land prices in Shanghai are not only drastically lower compared to before the January 28th Incident, but also no one is even inquiring about them. Regulations on interest rates for immovable property should not exceed 5%: Article 45 of the Provisional Constitution states, 'Usurious loans and excessively high rents for immovable property shall be prohibited by law.' This clear provision shows that excessive rents for immovable property are prohibited by law. In addition, the Civil Code has restricted interest rates on loans to no more than 5% and prohibits usury through criminal law. Furthermore, the government has recently ordered the reduction of interest rates on deposits and loans to alleviate the market situation, so interest rates on immovable property should not exceed 5%, which is permitted by law. Elimination of the rent collection system: One reason for the abnormally high rents in Shanghai is the speculation of rent collectors, who repeatedly raise rents. For example, if someone's property generates 10,000 yuan in rent per month, someone else is willing to lease it for 12,000 yuan. Therefore, rent collection is a mechanism for extracting rent from tenants and should be clearly prohibited and strictly eliminated. Reassessment of land and property values: Before the January 28th Incident, land prices in Shanghai were high due to commercial prosperity. Since the January 28th Incident, commerce has declined, and people's purchasing power is weak, so land prices should also decrease accordingly, which is reasonable. Therefore, reassessing land values is the only way to resolve the rent reduction issue. At the same time, the municipal authorities should fairly assess the value of buildings and regulate interest rates so that owners do not arbitrarily increase rents. Levy of vacant house tax: Property tax is used to subsidize municipal expenses, so all constructed houses should bear the obligation to pay taxes. The Shanghai authorities do not levy property tax on vacant houses, so owners can maintain high property prices and keep them closed. If a vacant house tax is levied, it can also help subsidize municipal expenses and suppress rents, which is a matter of urgency. Limit the construction period for vacant land: Shanghai is a major city in the East, and it is observed by all countries. Therefore, municipal construction is closely related to international affairs. Due to the current economic downturn, vacant land is abundant and has not yet been constructed, which is related to social recovery. The construction period should be limited to promote prosperity. Lease contracts should be invalidated: Legal changes should shift with social evolution. The market is on the verge of collapse, and it is difficult to restore it to its original state in a short period of time. This cannot be salvaged by human effort. Therefore, the lease contracts previously signed between tenants and owners should not be bound by them during this time of social difficulty and should be declared invalid. Please instruct that provisional attachment and provisional execution should not be abused: Legal provisions state that provisional attachment should not be granted unless there is a risk that compulsory execution will be impossible or very difficult in the future. There are clear restrictions. Therefore, in cases of litigation due to rent reduction, the responsibility for rent arrears should not be entirely borne by the tenant. According to the rent reduction steps prescribed by this committee, if rent is not reduced, rent will not be paid, and the rent will be deposited in a bank. Therefore, although there are rent arrears, there is no significant difficulty in execution. Therefore, the court's implementation of provisional attachment or provisional execution has a significant social impact. The Three Principles of the People of the late Premier of this party place the greatest emphasis on the Principle of People's Livelihood, and the four major needs of the Principle of People's Livelihood should be listed and emphasized equally. Today, the citizens of Shanghai are suffering greatly from the housing problem, and its impact has far-reaching consequences. Seeing this situation with our own eyes is heartbreaking, and it is difficult to remain silent. Therefore, we submit this document and humbly request that you consider the suffering of the citizens, quickly order the establishment of clear standards to alleviate the current situation, and relieve the people from their difficulties. We are extremely grateful. Respectfully submitted to Jiang, President of the Executive Yuan."

Residents of Hardoon's Properties Held a Meeting and Spoke Yesterday; Sent a Letter Urging the Landlord to Reduce Rent by 40%; Will Stop Paying Rent If the Goal Is Not Achieved 103

According to the Xin Xin She (New New News Agency), the Hardoon's Property Tenants Association held a joint meeting at 2:00 PM yesterday, with representatives from various lanes including Nanjing Road, Yunnan Road, Cishu Lane, Guangxi Road, Mingzhi Lane, Hankou Road, Cihou Lane, Zhejiang Road, Ciqing Lane, Fuxu Road, Cihui Lane, Sichuan Road, Cichang Lane, Wanjing Road, Ci [character missing] Lane, Cihe Lane, Ciqing Lane, and Cide Lane, totaling more than 200 people. Resolutions

After the usual formalities, the chairman reported on the purpose of the meeting and then discussed the following resolutions: The name and location of the association should be determined. Resolutions: (A) The name is determined to be the Hardoon's Property Tenants Association. (B) The office will be temporarily located at the Municipal Rent Reduction Association. How should the association proceed? Resolutions: Fill out volunteer forms on a household basis and establish the association on a scheduled basis. Determine the negotiation steps. Resolutions: (A) Send a letter stating the organizational process. (B) Send a letter urging the landlord to voluntarily reduce the rent by 40%. (C) Declare the cancellation of the previously signed contracts. The association should issue a declaration and ask various organizations to provide sympathy and assistance. Resolutions: Passed. What preparations should be made if there is no satisfactory response? Resolutions: (A) Unanimously stop paying rent. (B) Deposit the rent in the bank on a monthly basis. (C) Tenants with fixed-term leases should jointly publish a statement declaring the cancellation of unequal contracts. (D) Hire legal counsel to seek legal remedies. How should lawsuits be handled in the future? Resolutions: (A) All tenants of Hardoon's property will be legally protected by the association and file counterclaims. (B) Litigation costs will be borne by each tenant. How to expand publicity? Resolutions: Publish a special issue and print slogans for publicity. The meeting adjourned after the discussion.

Declaration

The association issued a declaration yesterday, stating: Shanghai is a major port in southeastern China, connecting China and foreign countries. It has a large population and its commerce has always been prosperous. However, since January 28th (Shanghai Incident) and for the past four or five years, rural areas have gone bankrupt, financial institutions have collapsed, and the social economy has deteriorated. Commerce has declined and the situation is increasingly dangerous. People of conscience in Shanghai, with a sense of hunger and drowning, seek to save the situation. Therefore, the issue of rent reduction has arisen, benefiting both parties without bias. After the beginning, tenants separately negotiated rent reductions with landlords. In general, wise landlords, understanding the principle of co-existence and co-prosperity, have implemented the meaning of sharing happiness and hardship, and have successively accepted requests, appropriately reduced rents, and reasonably resolved the issue. Only Hardoon Foreign Company, as a giant in the real estate industry, with houses all over various districts, and with tenants who are relatively well-off, occupying important locations, and charging high rents, the tenants have been petitioning for nearly a year. Not only have they not considered the friendship between the landlord and the tenant, but they have also taken many destructive and oppressive actions, including attachments and forced executions. The tenants are forced to convene a joint meeting of the Shanghai Rent Reduction Committee on February 17th. On the spot, it was unanimously decided to establish the Hardoon's Property Tenants Association of the Shanghai Rent Reduction Committee, so that they can work together to deal with the situation. If Hardoon Foreign Company can realize the situation and voluntarily reduce the rent by 40%, then commerce will recover in the future, the city will be revived, and prosperity will return. Both the landlord and the tenant will benefit from it. We can only hope for the best. The tenants will only deposit the rent due in the bank and wait for the resolution of the rent reduction. If the goal is not achieved, we vow not to pay rent to deal with the situation. We hope that the gentlemen of the country will correct us in our sincere intentions.

Residents of Hejiajiao Request Exemption from House Tax; Went to the Police Station Yesterday Afternoon to Request the Release of Detained Persons; Assembled at the Entire Residence This Morning to Petition the Municipal Government 105

Hejiajiao in the Fahua District of western Shanghai is located in a remote rural area, and most of the residents are farmers. The Municipal Finance Bureau decided to levy house tax in rural villages such as Hejiajiao in Fahua, which aroused opposition from the residents there. The reasons given were that roads have not been built (only concession roads), and there are no sanitation facilities or other equipment. Rural people live in their own houses and there are no markets except for one or two small teahouses and grocery stores. Moreover, in recent years, agriculture has declined, and it is difficult for residents to maintain their clothing and food, so how can they afford to increase their burden? The residents had previously submitted a petition to the Municipal Finance Bureau for exemption, but a few days ago, a collector from the Municipal West Collection Office went to the home of Yang Ma Shi at No. 2 Hejiajiao to collect house tax and took Yang to the police station, where he was released after paying a fine. Yesterday afternoon, the collector led the police to Yang's house to urge the payment of house tax and detained Yang Wenbin, a resident of No. 19, and Yang Ma Shi of No. 2, and押候解局訊辦。 Residents of the entire residence were informed and spontaneously assembled, flocking to the Xujiahui Police Station to petition. Director Yi Gongding saw that there were a large number of people and feared that it would cause trouble, so he sent Officer Hu to persuade the residents to maintain order. The China Merchants Bureau Held Qualification Examinations Yesterday; Director Lu Earnestly Explained the Purpose of the Qualification Examination; All Staff Members Expressed Their Acceptance of the Examination Method 110

Central News Agency reports that the state-run China Merchants Bureau, in order to reorganize its internal structure and economize on routine expenses, had the Ministry of Transportation stipulate qualification examination methods, with the aim of eliminating some redundant personnel. The staff, however, unanimously requested exemption from the exam, which prevented it from proceeding as scheduled. Yesterday, the chief examiners again earnestly explained the matter to all staff members, who have now expressed their acceptance. Details are recorded as follows:

All Staff Members Request Exemption from Examination

The Ministry of Transportation's qualification examination method for the bureau's staff was originally scheduled for written tests on the 16th, 17th, and 18th. Due to the staff's request for exemption, and their expressed intention to resign en masse, Chief Examiner Director Lu and others decided to provide a further earnest explanation to all staff, hoping they would comply with the Ministry's orders, consider the overall situation, and strive for the development of the bureau's affairs. They also announced a postponement of the examination.

Memorial Week Speech: Mr. Bo-ying Tan Reports

Director Lu and others originally intended to explain the gist of the Ministry of Transportation's qualification examination to all staff during the bureau's memorial week ceremony yesterday morning. However, due to General Manager Cai's attendance at the Municipal Land Bureau's memorial week ceremony, and Director Lu's and the other chief examiners' commitment to other official duties, they were unable to attend. Therefore, Deputy Manager Tan led the memorial week ceremony, announcing that a discussion meeting with all staff would be held in the afternoon.

Staff Discussion Meeting Convened in the Afternoon

At 3:00 PM, all staff members of the bureau gathered in the auditorium. General Manager Cai, accompanied by Lu Hanqin, Director of the Navigation Department of the Ministry of Transportation; Peng Hu, Director of the Navigation Bureau; and other examiners dispatched by the Ministry, met with the staff. General Manager Cai first introduced Director Lu, who again explained the Ministry of Transportation's qualification examination method to his colleagues. Subsequently, Director Lu gave a detailed explanation, and Director Peng, speaking as a former colleague (Director Peng served as the Chief of the General Affairs Section during General Manager Liu's tenure), offered encouragement to his colleagues. His words were extremely sincere.

Director Lu's Earnest Explanation

Director Lu first presented to all staff members the Ministry of Transportation's intention to reorganize the China Merchants Bureau, and the importance of the bureau's position in the domestic shipping industry. He then explained that the qualification examination stipulated by the Ministry of Transportation was based on the fairest method of selecting talent. He hoped that all staff members could understand the authorities' difficulties and work together to overcome the challenges. Finally, he guaranteed with his personal integrity that the China Merchants Bureau would not hire any new staff, nor would it employ any private individuals. Furthermore, after the qualification examination, those who were laid off would be given priority for re-employment when the bureau needed to add staff.

Staff Members Vote to Accept the Examination

After the reports from Manager Cai, Director Lu, and Director Peng, the staff members held a meeting in the auditorium to make a final vote on the Ministry of Transportation's qualification examination method. With unanimous agreement, they expressed their acceptance, and the matter came to a conclusion. An announcement was then made to adjourn the meeting.

Individual Interviews Held Yesterday and Today

After the meeting, at 4:00 PM, Director Lu, General Manager Cai, and the other examiners convened in the General Manager's office to discuss and decide to immediately invite each staff member for individual interviews. It was also announced that all office hours would be temporarily extended to 6:00 PM, and all staff members waited in their offices for the interview. However, due to the large number of people and the limited time, the individual interviews will continue today.

The Judicial Yuan Interprets Doubts Regarding Mortgage Rights; Auctioning Land with No Disputes; Transfer of Possession Required for Pledge of Machinery 111

The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce, the Bankers' Association, and the Native Bankers' Guild previously submitted a petition to the Executive Yuan to encourage the circulation of real estate in Shanghai, requesting the issuance of specific regulations to assist industry and commerce. The Executive Yuan convened the Ministries of Interior, Finance, Industry, and Judicial Administration to review the matter. The Executive Yuan then consulted the Judicial Yuan for a re-interpretation of Interpretation No. 493. The Judicial Yuan has now responded to the Executive Yuan with the following interpretation:

Regarding the matter of consultation, your esteemed Yuan's inquiry dated September 6th of last year, Document No. 245, concerning doubts regarding the applicability of Article 873, Paragraph 1, and Article 862, Paragraph 1, of the Civil Code, requesting clarification and a response, has been resolved by the Unified Interpretation of Laws and Regulations Conference of this Yuan.

Before the implementation of the registration laws stipulated in the Property Rights Section of the Civil Code, when a mortgagee whose debt has reached the repayment period but has not been repaid petitions the court to auction the mortgaged property, if the debtor or a third party does not dispute the mortgage relationship, there is no need to go through a judgment procedure, and the auction can proceed directly. This is not affected by whether or not a land registration system has been implemented.

In addition to being regarded as an accessory to the factory and mortgaged at the same time as the factory, the factory's machinery can also be regarded as an object of the factory. If only the machinery is mortgaged without transferring possession, according to Article 885, Paragraph 1, of the Civil Code, it cannot have the effect of a pledge until a Factory Mortgage Law is enacted.

Lu Shaotang's Appeal Against Embezzlement is Concluded 121

Sentencing Scheduled for the 24th of This Month

Lu Shaotang, a real estate businessman from Suzhou living in Shanghai, formerly served as the manager of the Suzhou branch of the China General Chamber of Commerce Bank and also founded the Guixing Real Estate Company in Shanghai. Unexpectedly, in recent years, he was affected by the economic downturn, which caused him severe hardship. He and his son, Lu Bingsheng, the associate manager of the Suzhou branch of the China General Chamber of Commerce Bank, embezzled and used 500,000 yuan of banknotes from the Shanghai office of the China General Chamber of Commerce Bank, which was stored in the Guixing Real Estate Company. Although part of it was returned, as much as 239,000 yuan was still owed. It was not until the spring of last year that Chuan Xiaoyan, the chairman of the China General Chamber of Commerce Bank, discovered it and found solid evidence. He reported it to the Central Police Station of the Public Concession, requesting that the First Special District Court issue an arrest warrant and instruct detectives to arrest him. Lu Shaotang had already fled after hearing the news, and only his son Bingsheng was arrested, sent to court, and sentenced to one year and six months in prison for embezzlement, and ordered to repay the plaintiff's 239,000 yuan. The case had already been finalized after three trials. Lu Shaotang also surrendered to the police station last month and was sent to the First Special District Court for trial, sentenced to one year and six months in prison, suspended for two years, and ordered to jointly and severally repay the plaintiff's 239,000 yuan with Lu Bingsheng. Lu refused to accept the judgment and appealed to the Second Branch of the Jiangsu High Court. Yesterday afternoon, Presiding Judge Yu Hua and Judges Kai Zhong and Zhou jointly heard the case. The appellant, accompanied by lawyers Zhang Shizhao and Yang Linzhi, appeared and presented reasons, requesting that the original judgment be revoked and declared innocent. After the court investigated for a long time, and the appellant's agent and the police station's agent, lawyer Gan Jingxian, exchanged arguments, the court ruled that the argument in this case was over and scheduled the judgment to be announced on the afternoon of the 24th of this month.

Yiye Haitien Employed in Tianjin, Plaintiff Requests Letter to Transfer to Tianjin

The branches and sub-branches of the Wuhua Bank in this city closed simultaneously on August 20th two years ago. So far, although the Wuhua Head Office in Hong Kong has sent people to Shanghai to assist in the liquidation, there is still no progress, causing creditors of the Shanghai branch to file civil and criminal lawsuits against those responsible with the Second Special District Local Court, either to recover the embezzled funds or to request legal punishment. Last month, depositors of the branch, such as Kong Zhongqi, filed a lawsuit with the First Special District Local Court against the Shanghai branch's advisors Zeng, Chen Bingqian, Cui Pingxi, Branch Manager Fan Shaoliang, Deputy Manager Ye Haitien, Branch Manager Wang Jian, and Deputy Manager Wu Yousan for

fraud and breach of trust. After the summons, many defendants did not appear, so it was postponed, as recorded in this newspaper. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Dai Rongduo reopened the court. The plaintiffs included Kong Zhongqi, Gu Shide, Ma Yimin, and representatives of the Miaoji Company. Guo Xingsheng, Sun Yanji, and Ren Yao did not appear either. deposited in the branch, for a total of over 3,400 yuan, and submitted evidence such as deposit books and checks. Defendant Chen Bingqian testified that he was hired as an advisor when the branch opened, but did not receive a salary. In 1934, he returned to Guangdong and resigned. The nature of the advisor was similar to that of a consultant, only for consultation. Cui Pingxi admitted to being one of the nine advisors, but never advised on the bank's affairs and did not receive a salary. The defense attorney for Wu Yousan stated on Wu's behalf that Wu, although he served as the deputy manager of the sub-branch, did not clearly understand

the reasons for the closing of the branch. The court then questioned Wang Jian. Wang testified that the name of the advisory committee was a special product of Guangdong, and there were no clear regulations in the law, so he did not understand his powers. However, the committee issued orders to the branch's managers and deputies. The branch's capital was set at 500,000, half of which was allocated by the head office, and the rest was raised by Fan and Ye. After the closing, it was learned that the amount raised was still insufficient, and 220,000 of the funds allocated by the head office had been withdrawn before the closing. The sub-branch was an agency for the branch's collection and payment.

No Independence, therefore no capital. Each plaintiff then stated that Ye Haitien is currently the deputy manager of the Guohua Bank in Tianjin and requested that a letter be sent to the Tianjin court for assistance. The defendants' lawyers stated that the nature of the case was the same as the case managed by the Second Special District Court and requested that the file be transferred from the Second Special District Court for verification to facilitate understanding. Judge Dai then ordered that the hearing be rescheduled to the afternoon of the 28th of this month.

Taxpayers Association Appeals for Severe Punishment of Tax Collection Staff for Disturbances 126

Xie Xingxiang and others appeal to the Ningbo Association

The Public Concession Taxpayers Association has sent a letter to the Shanghai Municipal Council (工部局) regarding the Western tax collectors who forcibly collected the spring general tax from businesses such as Xie Xingxiang on Xinji Bang Road in Hongkou. They allegedly rushed upstairs, caused disturbances, and beat people indiscriminately. The association requests the Municipal Council to severely punish the staff to ensure business stability. The original letter stated: "To the Ningbo Association in Shanghai: We, Xie Xingxiang and other businesses on Xinji Bang Road in Hongkou, have paid the general tax and patrol fees to the Municipal Council on time every quarter. Recently, we renovated our premises last year. Due to the landlord raising the rent, we are requesting a rent reduction, which is currently in court. Therefore, we pay the general tax at the end of each quarter, pending the resolution of the rent reduction, after which the general tax should be adjusted accordingly. Unexpectedly, on the 8th of this month at 9 am, the Municipal Council sent a Western tax collector to forcibly collect the spring general tax. He rushed upstairs into the bedrooms and beat people indiscriminately, even shop customers were affected. If a citizen refuses to pay tax, there is a court of law or the Municipal Council where the authorities can file a complaint. How can such barbaric methods be used? It is intolerable! We have always admired your association for upholding justice. We earnestly request that you forward this letter to the Municipal Council, requesting severe punishment for the tax collector." After investigating, the Council's staff should show proper courtesy to businesses. The inappropriate actions of the tax collector should be punished to serve as a warning. We have sent a special letter to your association, requesting that you forward it to the Municipal Council, severely punishing the tax collector to appease public sentiment and stabilize business. After deliberation by the association, it was decided that, as the businesses are currently involved in a rent reduction lawsuit and are delaying the payment of the general tax, your bureau's tax collectors should only advise them to pay at the previous rate first. After the lawsuit is resolved, the amount of the general tax can be determined, and the difference can be either refunded or offset. There is absolutely no reason to harass households. Based on the previous letter, we request that your bureau promptly instruct the relevant authorities to investigate the offending staff member and punish him to ensure business stability. This is addressed to the Chief of the Shanghai Municipal Council of the Public Concession.

1935 Public Concession Health Overview 127

Reduction in infectious diseases, only three deaths from smallpox

Cholera hasn't appeared for three years, malaria is a growing concern

Hospital expansion is limited by financial constraints

School medical work focused on Chinese elementary schools

The 1935 report of the Director of the Health Department of the Municipal Council has been submitted to the Board of Directors. As the original text is quite long, we have extracted the key points and translated them into Chinese for your preliminary review.

General Situation in Shanghai: According to the report of the Director of the Health Department, the public health situation in the Public Concession in 1935 can be considered satisfactory. Since 1926, no severe epidemics have been discovered in Shanghai. True cholera has not occurred in Shanghai for three consecutive years. However, this disease is unpredictable, so the Concession authorities must continue to implement preventive and isolation measures to prevent its recurrence. Scarlet fever has gradually decreased in recent years. However, in 1935, it gradually increased again. According to the Director of the Health Department, the government has done its best in terms of prevention, such as strict inspection of beverages and food and mandatory disinfection. What has not yet been achieved is personal hygiene and prevention, which depends on close cooperation between citizens and health authorities. Furthermore, the Concession health authorities are now viewing the latent growth of malaria as a hidden worry. This may be due to the advancement of transportation and the fact that citizens move to the countryside in the summer. To cut off the source of malaria, it is essential to eliminate mosquitoes. The Concession authorities' experiments on removing mosquito larvae have shown some success. According to statistics, in 1935, 122 foreign residents in the Concession contracted malaria and were reported, fortunately, none died. 291 Chinese residents contracted malaria and were reported, with as many as 15 deaths. The prevention of smallpox seems to be deeply understood by all residents in the Concession. More than 300,000 residents in the Concession were vaccinated that year. This is another record of the work of the Health Department. It is also heard that the number of vaccinations on the birthday of the Flower Goddess reached more than 25,000, which shows how much Chinese citizens value flowers. However, the number of people receiving cholera vaccinations has decreased sharply. Only 198,000 people were vaccinated that year, and more than 10,000 people received revaccinations. In addition, the number of cases of rabies in dogs within the Concession has greatly increased. Although the police authorities have tried their best to eradicate this disease, their authority is limited and cannot extend beyond the Concession, which is regrettable. This year, 19 citizens died from rabies, 16 of whom were not residents of the Concession.

Birth and Death Statistics: The registration of infant births in the Public Concession is considered complete for foreign residents. However, for Chinese residents, although the number of infant births registered has increased, it is likely still far from the actual number. 20,567 Chinese infants were reported to be born in the Concession, including 10,983 males and 9,584 females. 891 foreign infants were born, including 448 males and 443 females. This year, 13,429 Chinese died, with old age being the biggest cause of death, followed by pulmonary tuberculosis, brain disease, and typhoid fever. 606 foreigners died in the Public Concession, 488 of whom were residents of the Concession, with non-Chinese Asians accounting for more than half. Furthermore, a census was conducted again this year, which will further increase the accuracy of birth and death statistics.

Hospital Work: The Director of the Health Department stated that due to economic difficulties this year, the department's original hospital and other construction plans could not be realized as scheduled. However, the development of hospital facilities outside the Concession is still gratifying. It is hoped that this suspension of construction will not be permanent, as the buildings of the bureau's hospitals are already dilapidated and cannot be used. Fortunately, there have been no severe epidemics in Shanghai in recent years, so they can barely be maintained. However, it is feared that extreme prosperity will turn into adversity, so it is necessary to plan ahead. The current hospital work in the Public Concession is divided into three categories: Public Health Services, Bureau Medical Services, and Other. Public Health Services include tuberculosis sanatoriums, venereal disease hospitals for foreign men, vaccinations, and inoculations. Bureau Medical Services include hospitals for police officers and prisoners, health lectures for police and fire department personnel, physical examinations for civil servants upon employment, health propaganda for various departments, and the Moganshan Sanatorium. In terms of infectious diseases, the situation this year is extremely satisfactory. The absence of cholera has already been mentioned. This year, the number of patients in the fever hospital was 1,409, a decrease of 30% compared to the more than 2,000 in the previous year. Only 41 people with smallpox were admitted to the hospital, with 3 deaths. In the previous year, there were 369 patients and 135 deaths. It is unknown whether this good situation can be maintained this year. What is currently lacking in Shanghai is insufficient equipment for tuberculosis treatment centers. The new fever and neuropsychiatric hospital has been suspended due to economic reasons. There is also a lack of dental equipment for poor citizens, resulting in an increasing number of women and children suffering from dental diseases. The facilities of the children's convalescent home should also be added. Regarding prison hospital work, the Western prison has been moved to a new location, and hygiene facilities have greatly improved compared to before. Among the prisoners, except for four who required surgery, all suffered from minor ailments. Two people were moved to the isolation ward, and two suffered from mental illness. There were no deaths. The situation in the Chinese prison has also improved compared to before. A major reform in hygiene is the abolition of the previous cleaning coolies and their replacement with 12 fully trained nurses.

Food Inspection: In terms of food and beverage cleanliness, there has also been significant progress in 1935. Milk prices have gradually fallen, but the degree of cleanliness has increased. In the future, Grade B milk will also be disinfected uniformly. This measure is unlikely to encounter any obstacles. After the opening of the Eastern District Bureau Slaughterhouse, meat inspection has gradually become unified. This can also be said to be a major advance in municipal health. However, many butchers are still bound by old habits and have not been able to apply this mechanical operation appropriately. The food samples inspected this year included flour, bread, butter, margarine, cheese, glucose, milk sugar, milk powder, flaxseed, sausage, condensed milk, etc. The beverages inspected included whiskey, beer, alcohol, vodka, various sodas, fruit juices, fruit露, etc. The general situation is still good. The malpractice of milk adulteration has decreased compared to before.

School Health: The Shanghai Municipal Council's school medical and health work is divided into three major parts: Bureau-run schools, Bureau-run Chinese elementary schools, and grant-aided schools within the Concession. The first category, Bureau-run schools, refers to the Chinese and Western middle schools for boys and girls. Due to economic constraints, the bureau has not been able to fully provide the necessary medical services to these schools. What can be done is only the cleanliness of school buildings and drinking water. The most important work in 1935 was to establish temporary clinics and conduct trachoma examinations, centered on five Chinese elementary schools. However, due to the lack of medical staff, the clinics could not be permanently established, so the recovery of those suffering from trachoma was delayed. This year, 1,967 elementary school students were examined, with 1,143 suffering from eye diseases, 442 suffering from skin diseases, 864 suffering from heart defects, 393 suffering from lung weakness, 1,252 suffering from tonsillitis, and 89 suffering from poor eyesight. The reason why so many children suffer from heart disease is probably because they do not have enough time to recuperate after illness, even if they return to school. Regarding grant-aided Chinese private schools, 2,363 inspections were conducted this year. Generally, due to the current economic depression, the overcrowding of these schools is the most difficult problem. Schools that used to have good hygiene conditions are now no longer good, mostly because there are too many students and the classrooms are not well-ventilated. Some have expanded their school buildings, while others are limited by the site and cannot be expanded. This issue is currently being specially studied by the health authorities.

Summer Work: The Municipal Council Health Department has special work to do every summer. In terms of beverages, the results of inspections of various fruit juices sold by street vendors mostly show that they are not fit for human consumption. Those transporting ice cream are given appropriate permits to distinguish them from other private sellers. Fly control is also one of the summer work items. All major hotels and restaurants are inspected from time to time to ensure that they have fly-killing equipment. All 13 soda factories in Shanghai must also be inspected from time to time. In addition, mosquito control, garbage management, and swimming pool cleanliness are also part of the department's summer work.

Typhoid Fever Outbreak Among Japanese Residents on Shigaota Road 128

The Japanese-language Daily News reports that the area around Shigaota Road at the end of North Sichuan Road in Shanghai is mostly inhabited by Japanese. Recently, there has been a severe outbreak of typhoid fever, with most of the patients being Japanese. There are already more than ten cases, causing panic among nearby residents, and there is a risk of it spreading. For example, Yamazaki Aiko, the wife of a Japanese grocery store owner, fell ill four or five days ago. Yacun, who works at the grocery store, also contracted typhoid fever (i.e., severe typhoid fever) two or three days ago. Both are currently being treated at Suzuki Hospital. In addition, the wife and female servant of an employee of a Japanese spinning mill have also been diagnosed with severe typhoid fever by Fumin Hospital. However, the source of this infection is still unknown. The police of the Japanese Consulate General are sending personnel to investigate the cause and are also forcing residents in the vicinity to get vaccinated. The incubation period for this disease is about ten days. If fever and diarrhea occur, it is difficult to treat, so it is best to get vaccinated as a precaution.

Husband Has An Affair, Family Provokes A Tragic Change: Wife Takes Poison and Then Orders Two Sons to Swallow It - Accused of Instigating Murder But Mitigating Circumstances Exist - Judge Advises Bao Jianfu to Eliminate Disputes 132

Bao Jianfu from Chongming, in his forties, used to be a broker at the Commodities Exchange. He closed down his business some years ago and is now employed at the East Asia Bank at 299 Sichuan Road. His home is located at No. 7, Lane 240, Hart Road in western Shanghai. He married a woman surnamed Hu, who is the same age and from the same hometown as Bao. They have two sons, the eldest named Zhigang, who is 13 years old and studies at Yucai Public School on Carter Road, and the younger one named Zhijiong, who is only 9 years old and attends Peiren Elementary School on Xiaoshadu Road. Bao also has an elderly father who is supported at home. The three generations live together, and the family was originally very harmonious. However, Bao has had a concubine named Tang for several years. Although Yin and Xing have always avoided each other, Bao's love is clearly not focused, so Mrs. Hu often clashes with him. On December 11th of last year, Bao took a refrigerator from home to his concubine's place, which caused Mrs. Hu to be very angry and quarrel with him. The next morning at 8 o'clock, Mrs. Hu bought opium and swallowed it herself. She placed the remaining four small bags on the table in the bedroom and told her two sons to take medicine after drinking porridge and then go to school. After the two sons finished their meal and entered the room, Mrs. Hu had already collapsed on the bed. They each took two bags of opium and swallowed them before going to school. Before long, Mrs. Hu's poison took effect in her abdomen. Her family notified Bao Jianfu by phone, who rushed home and took her by car to the Red Cross Hospital on Haig Road for treatment. As soon as Mrs. Hu left the house, the two children, Zhigang and Zhijiong, were successively sent back by people from their respective schools. Bao hired a doctor to examine them and found that they had also been poisoned. He also urgently sent them to the Red Cross Hospital for treatment. The hospital received three members of the mother and sons family within a short period of time.

The matter was extremely shocking.

They immediately reported it to the Jing'an Temple Police Station, which sent Detective Niao Chengjun and a Western detective to investigate. Fortunately, the two children had only ingested a small amount of poison, and after five days of treatment, they all recovered and were taken home by their father. However, Mrs. Bao Hu had ingested more poison and had a history of mental illness, so she had not yet recovered and remained in the hospital. However, the police station believed that Mrs. Hu's suicide was already extremely unwise, and that she had even tried to take her two sons with her, which was very absurd in terms of human reason and law. Therefore, they filed a lawsuit for suicide and

Instigating Suicide

in the First Special District District Court. Yesterday morning, Judge Liu Yugui opened the court and ordered Bao Hu to be brought to court for interrogation. Bao Jianfu also brought his two sons to court. First, Zhang Dayin, the lawyer for the police station, stated the course of events, saying that the defendant must have been afraid that after her suicide, her two sons would become motherless children, so she took this action to die together. He also presented the hospital diagnosis report and Zhigang's confession written in the hospital, stating that his mother had ordered him and his brother to swallow opium. The court then summoned Bao Zhigang to testify about

The Circumstances of Poisoning.

Zhigang no longer claimed that the poisoning was on his mother's orders, only saying that his mother had only told him and his brother to take medicine, so they thought that what was on the table was medicine, and they each took two small pieces and swallowed them. After arriving at the hospital, he was in a state of mental confusion and did not know what he was doing, only feeling sleepy. His younger brother, Zhijiong, said almost the same thing. Judge Liu asked Mrs. Bao Hu, who mostly did not answer. Judge Liu then instructed Bao Jianfu, saying that the three lives in this case had all been saved, which was fortunate. Although

The Reasons for Suicide

had not been stated in detail, it was clear that it stemmed from family disputes. You should find a way to eliminate the disputes to avoid future troubles. He ordered the debate to begin, and first the lawyer for the police station spoke, saying that the defendant's suicide and instigation of suicide were a premeditated plan. In order to prevent such incidents from happening in the future, she should be warned. However, considering that it was due to great provocation, her situation was still worthy of pity and forgiveness, and it seemed appropriate to announce a suspended sentence. The lawyer for the defendant, Jiang Baoli, made a defense, and the court adjourned to pronounce the verdict on Wednesday. Bao Hu was ordered to be taken back by her husband, Bao Jianfu.

Exploiting Customs House Doorways: Con Artists Show Their Skills - Fraudulent Cases of Entering from the Front Door and Exiting from the Back Door Are Repeated - Shen Jinsheng Arrested for Committing Ten Offenses 133

In addition to the main gate facing the Huangpu River, the Customs House on the Bund in Hankou Road has two back doors on Hankou Road and Sichuan Road, which do not restrict others from entering. Therefore, those who are not related to the Customs House can also freely enter and exit through these three doors. As a result, some people have taken advantage of this opportunity to fraudulently purchase goods from various shops, asking the shops to send someone to deliver the goods to the Customs House and then collect payment. The con artist waits in the Customs House in advance, takes the goods from the deliverer's hands, pretends to go inside to get money, and then escapes through the back door. Similar fraud cases have been seen many times. Recently, a certain aviation lottery sales office was defrauded of 20 yuan of lottery tickets, a certain watch shop was defrauded of an electric meter worth 10 yuan, and a certain Guangdong shop was defrauded of 20 yuan of sausage. All were delivered to the Customs House, and then the con artists disappeared. Yesterday morning at 9 o'clock, a man went to Shenglong Grocery Store on Hengbang Bridge, North Sichuan Road, and bought five catties of slender sausage, two catties of oily fish, four cans of milk, four cans of canned abalone, and four cans of salted fish, worth a total of 16 yuan and 64 cents. He also asked the store to deliver the goods to Mr. Li's office on the second floor of the Customs House to hand over the goods and collect the money. The store sent a Cantonese employee, Liang Xi, to deliver the goods to the Customs House and went directly to the second floor, searching everywhere for Mr. Li without success. When he returned to the escalator, he saw the person who had previously purchased the goods approaching and taking the goods, telling Liang to wait a moment at the door to get the money. At the same time, he carried the goods and wanted to escape. He was discovered by Plainclothes Chinese Detective No. 87 of the Customs House Marine Police, who was serving in the Customs House. The witness and the person were taken to the Marine Police Station. The defendant was identified as Shen Jinsheng, 30 years old, from Guangdong. He spoke fluent Shanghainese and admitted to defrauding the plaintiff of the goods. After checking his fingerprints, it was discovered that in July of the 22nd year of the Republic of China, the defendant wore a white uniform with copper buttons and rented a room in a certain hotel, posing as a customs officer. After becoming familiar with the cashier, he falsely claimed that the Customs House was recruiting investigators with a high monthly salary. The cashier was deceived and gave him 50 yuan for "expenses." One day, he was led into the Customs House and told the cashier to take off his silk gown so that he could go upstairs to check his physique. In an instant, the defendant took the silk gown and disappeared. He was arrested by detectives from the Marine Police Station on the 11th of this month and sent to the District Court, where he was sentenced to one year in prison. The police station then verified his fingerprints with the Concession Police Station and discovered that the defendant had committed eight similar fraud cases in the territory. On December 26th of last year, he was just released from prison after serving a one-year sentence for fraud imposed by the Hongkou Police Station in the Special District Court. In less than two months, he was caught in the legal net again. He has committed a total of ten crimes and is extremely lawless. The police chief, having determined the interrogation was clear, ordered the detective to be sent to the District Court for questioning this morning.

Difficulty in Rapidly Implementing Interest Rate Reduction in the Banking Industry: The Banking Industry Subcommittee is Currently Studying the Matter Meticulously, and Will Consult with the Money Industry After a Concrete Plan is Available 134

Regarding the matter of reducing loan interest rates, rescuing industry and commerce, and prospering the market, the Bankers Association of this city has specially formed a subcommittee to conduct research. Yesterday morning, according to a reporter from the New News Agency who inquired with the banking community, the above matter is extremely complicated and cannot be quickly realized without considering all aspects. Although reducing loan interest rates is a good strategy for rescuing industry and commerce, the banking and money industries themselves cannot be disregarded. In terms of the current situation, bank deposit interest rates are mostly six percent, and loan interest rates are nine percent. In fact, it seems difficult to consider them excessively harsh. If loan interest rates are reduced in the future, then in order to maintain their own interests, deposit interest rates will also have to be appropriately reduced. Therefore, the Banking Association Subcommittee is currently conducting meticulous research. Once a concrete plan is drafted, it will be submitted to the Executive Committee for discussion and then consulted with representatives of the Money Industry Association. Then, the proposed plan will be submitted to the Ministry of Finance for review and approval. Therefore, reducing deposit and loan interest rates is difficult to achieve in the short term.

Tax Police Clash with Farmers: Trial Begins 135

Two police officers, Huang Zhifa and Wang Ming, from the 32nd Squad of the 4th District of the Huainan Tax Police stationed in Zhaozhen, Rugao, apprehended Ding Weiyong for selling smuggled salt on the beach on August 13th of last year. They surrounded Huang and Wang, severely beat them, tied them up with ropes inside a nearby land temple, and intended to kill them. One civilian, Cheng Shaoan, was slow to escape and was killed. Feng Rulin, Liu Kefu, and others were also wounded by gunfire. Zhou Fengxuan, accompanied by deputy leader Tu Rong, police officers Chen Jun, Tong Changpu, Fan Xianyu, and defense lawyer Ge Zhitan, appeared in court. Judge Tan questioned them extensively and determined that the case was extraordinarily complex. He adjourned the hearing for further investigation and released Zhou Fengxuan and others on bail.

China International Famine Relief Commission Appoints Advisory Committee Members for the Yangtze River Basin 139

The China International Famine Relief Commission, located at No. 505 Henan Road in this city, is a joint organization of Chinese and foreign philanthropists whose main purpose is to mitigate natural disasters in China. Since its establishment in 1921, the commission has conducted emergency relief and work relief projects throughout the country, spending over 50 million yuan. Its achievements have been widely praised by society. In 1931, when the Yangtze River flooded, the commission established the Yangtze River Basin Relief Advisory Committee to prevent and relieve disasters in the Yangtze River area. It hired experts to work together, with Mr. Chen Guangfu and Mr. Wu Liande serving as chairman and vice-chairman, respectively. Since its establishment, it has made significant contributions. Long-Term Unemployed Man Rescued After Jumping into Huangpu River 142

Around 1 p.m. yesterday, the Dongjiadu ferry, traveling from Puxi to Pudong, had reached the middle of the river when a passenger, taking advantage of the crowd, jumped into the river in an attempt to commit suicide. The ferry immediately stopped to rescue him. With the help of boatmen such as Chen Bao, he was fortunately rescued quickly because it was daytime. They reported the incident to the Shanghai Municipal Water Patrol Corps, which sent personnel to investigate. The man identified himself as Pu Yusheng, 24 years old, from Pudong, residing at No. 5 Pentang Lane, Xiaodongmen. He had resorted to this desperate act due to long-term unemployment and poverty. The Water Patrol notified his family to take him back and keep him under supervision.

Danyang Native Place Association in Shanghai Seeks Members: Opened Yesterday 148

Since moving to No. 14 Fangxie Road, the Danyang Native Place Association in Shanghai has been developing rapidly. After finding that there are nearly 30,000 Danyang natives in Shanghai, but less than one-tenth are members, the standing committee resolved to appoint He Yunsheng, Han Jingqi, Dong Kenqian, Pei Yuanding, Liu Zhemin, Hua Jun, Dai Yingfu, Zhu Xinru, Dai Xingcha, Dai Jinyong, Wang Jinwen, Xu Jinfa, Wang Qideng, Yue Xijin, and Zhang Mingyu to form a membership recruitment committee. After repeated meetings, He Yunsheng was elected as chairman, and Dai Jinyong as general captain. Zhu Xinru and over sixty others were appointed as team leaders to recruit members separately. The recruitment campaign was launched yesterday. All Danyang natives are welcome to join. The association's declaration and membership recruitment rules are listed below.

Declaration 149

At a time when a second world war is about to break out, and the tide of economic recession is affecting us first, we seem to hear the tragic cries of our compatriots in North China being slaughtered, and we seem to see the desolate scene after the raging torrents have washed over our homeland. In such a dangerous environment, we feel even more fortunate and concerned about the existence of the Native Place Association. We are not confined to narrow localism; this is the beginning of national unity. Without strong hometown ties, how can we talk about national consciousness? Without the virtue of mutual assistance, how can we talk about jointly facing national difficulties? We can only recognize our goals and start from the foundation. The history of the Danyang Native Place Association in Shanghai is very long. Through the efforts of many responsible individuals, it has gradually become sound. Everything is done according to the welfare of the majority. While thinking about the natives of Shanghai, we are always thinking about promoting the cause of our hometown. Indeed, we have many things we want to do but cannot achieve, and we feel even more lonely in our strength. We eagerly look forward to a new force, the entire native of Shanghai, to join this group and work hard. Everyone knows that unity is strength. Two simple examples will make it clear: the wind can uproot an isolated tree but cannot break the branches of a forest. The overbearing mantis cannot defeat a tiny ant colony. Fellow natives, when you first came to Shanghai, did you feel strange? After a busy day, do you feel monotonous? Are there many problems that you think you cannot solve alone? The Native Place Association can solve them for you satisfactorily. Hometown fathers, brothers, and sisters in Shanghai, come and join the Native Place Association! We sincerely welcome you. Spring has arrived, and we hope that the Native Place Association will also rise up with the times! The Danyang Native Place Association Recruitment Committee.

Recruitment Rules 150

Membership Recruitment Rules: 1. Recruitment Period: From February 15, 1936, to April 15, 1936. 2. Recruitment Structure: Provisionally set at 30 teams (may be added as necessary), each team with one team leader and one to two deputy team leaders, and one general captain. 3. Recruitment Target: Provisionally set at 3,000 points, 100 points per team, with one yuan in national currency equal to one point. 4. Rewards: The team with the highest score exceeding the assigned score will receive a large silver cup for first place, a silver cup for second place, and a small silver cup for third place. For individuals who exceed 50 points, the reward method is the same as above. If an individual scores over 500 points, they will receive a scroll of calligraphy by Mr. Ma Xiangbo, a member of the association, with a personally inscribed title. 5. Recruitment Procedure: When recruiting members, they must follow the association's constitution, be introduced by two or more members, fill out an application form, and pay the membership fee, which will be acknowledged with a receipt from the association and a membership card. 6. Team scores will be announced every 15 days to compare the progress of each team. 7. Membership qualifications and membership fee amounts are detailed in the association's application form. 8. Members are more than welcome to contribute special donations in addition to membership fees. 9. Special donations can also be counted towards recruitment scores. 10. The Recruitment Committee may revise these rules at any time if necessary.

Mother Abuses Young Child: Police Investigate and Prosecute 151

Zhang Shen, a local woman, 30 years old, married Zhang Jinshi, a Ningbo native, and lived at No. 95 Gujia Lane, Luban Road, French Concession. She has two sons, Lian'gen, 6 years old, and Lianfa, 3 years old. Zhang Jinbao works as a steward on a ship and does not often return home. Recently, for unknown reasons, Shen has been severely abusing her youngest son, Lianfa, causing him to be covered in bruises. Xu Guilin, a detective from the French police, found out about the matter and brought Shen and the child to the police station. After questioning, the police chief ordered Shen to be detained and the injured child sent to Guangci Hospital for treatment. Yesterday afternoon, Shen was transferred to the First Criminal Court of the Second Special District. The police lawyer stated that the child was still in the hospital for treatment and requested an extension for further investigation. When questioned, Shen claimed that women do not dare to abuse, and her remaining statements were evasive. Judge Wang ordered Shen to pay a bail of 300 yuan and rescheduled the hearing for the afternoon of the 20th.

Shiye She reported that the Ministry of Finance Jiangsu Provincial Nitrate and Sulfur Bureau, because the Chile Nitrate Sales Office has been ordered to be taken back effective March 1, yesterday specially notified all users to first register their annual usage with the bureau before they can purchase. The notification stated, "After investigation, the Chile Nitrate Sales Office under this bureau will close at the end of February of this year. From March 1, all Chile nitrate sales matters will be taken back by this bureau for self-management, as ordered by the Ministry of Finance. In the future, all Chile nitrate users must first submit their annual needs to this bureau, which will be forwarded for approval and registration, before purchasing at the Chile Nitrate Sales Office of this bureau. In addition to reporting and sending letters, it is hereby announced in the newspaper for general knowledge."

Wang Wencheng (30 years old, from Tongzhou), the handcart puller pulling the rope in front, was run over and fell to the ground, suffering severe internal injuries. The National Physical Education Institute's Southern Expedition 164

Warmly Welcomed by Overseas Chinese in Various Locations. The Team Will Travel to Various Ports in Malaysia on the 9th for Performances.

The Central National Martial Arts Institute and the National Physical Education School are touring Southeast Asia to promote physical education and have been warmly welcomed by overseas Chinese. Pang Yusen, the leader of the school, recently returned to Shanghai and will go to Beijing tonight to report for duty. According to him, after the school finishes its performances in Southeast Asia, Principal Zhang will lead the team to the Philippines. Details are as follows:

Competition Schedule in the Philippines:

According to Pang, when the school's athletes passed through the Philippines, they paid a visit to the Chinese Overseas Chinese Basketball Association in the Philippines, as they had previously received a letter inviting them to compete. They also negotiated competition matters with the association's president, Li Lianchao. The competition schedule in the Philippines was immediately decided as follows: 1. University of the Philippines, 2. University of Santo Tomas, 3. National University, 4. San Beda College, 5. Far Eastern University, 6. De La Salle College, 7. Rizal University, 8. Chinese and Western Alumni Team, 9. Overseas Chinese Joint Team. All competition venues will be held at the Rizal Memorial Sports Complex. After the negotiations were completed, President Li led them on a tour of various places for a week, and then they boarded a ship to Singapore the next morning.

Five Wins in Five Matches in Singapore:

After six days at sea, the ship arrived in Singapore early on the 25th. At the dock, there were more than a dozen groups and hundreds of local dignitaries to welcome them. All team members stayed at the Kowloon Hall. The dates for the martial arts performances and basketball games were determined by the Chinese General Chamber of Commerce and the Basketball and Volleyball Association, starting from January 31st to February 6th. There were seven days of martial arts performances and five basketball games: February 1st against the Weiyang Basketball Team, February 2nd against the Gongshang Basketball Team, February 3rd free, February 4th against the Chongwu Basketball Team, February 5th against the Amateur Basketball Team, and February 6th against the Singapore Joint Team. Our team has already won all five matches, and the results are as follows: National Physical Education Institute vs. Weiyang, National Physical Education Institute 82, Weiyang 43; National Physical Education Institute vs. Gongshang, National Physical Education Institute 99, Gongshang 34; National Physical Education Institute vs. Chongwu, National Physical Education Institute 61, Chongwu 29; National Physical Education Institute vs. Amateur, National Physical Education Institute 51, Amateur 39; National Physical Education Institute vs. Singapore Joint Team, National Physical Education Institute 55, Singapore Joint Team 45.

Martial Arts Performances Attract Enthusiastic Audiences:

The martial arts performances also changed the program every day and were quite popular with the audience. To limit the audience and maintain order, the General Chamber of Commerce stipulated that tickets must be purchased for admission. There were four types of tickets: 50 cents, one yuan, two yuan, and three yuan. The venue could accommodate five or six thousand people, but it was still crowded every game, and the seats were not enough. On the last day, for the purpose of popularizing the performances, the martial arts performances were open to the public without tickets. However, three hours before the performance, the venue was already full and overflowing, and the order could not be maintained. The venue doors were closed, and no one was allowed to enter or exit. Those who arrived later were not able to enter, and they all lamented their missed opportunity. It can be seen that the overseas Chinese felt such interest in martial arts, and they must have had a good impression and a deep understanding of martial arts. Therefore, the publicity work for our country also had a considerable effect, which is gratifying.

Continuing Performances in Various Ports in Malaysia:

Our country, at the invitation of Kuala Lumpur, Jinbao, Ipoh, Penang, and other places in Malaysia, will be led by Director Zhang on the 9th of this month to perform martial arts and hold basketball games in various places. Because I had to take care of the affairs of the National Physical Education School, I could not stay overseas for a long time. Therefore, I took the Italian postal ship "Countervanth" on the 10th of this month and returned to China the day before yesterday, and I will return to Beijing to report for duty immediately. The duration of our country's trip to Southeast Asia has not yet been determined, because various islands in Southeast Asia have sent letters inviting us. For the sake of general publicity in Southeast Asia, it is not convenient to refuse. Our country will perform in Kuala Lumpur, Jinbao, Ipoh, Penang, and other places in Malaysia until about March 4th, and then go to Medan, Sumatra, and Java, Surabaya, and Batavia in the Dutch East Indies, and then return to Saigon and Manila.
