The 11th World Games: Closing Ceremony of the Winter Games 169

The Chairman of the International Committee Gave the Closing Remarks. The Venue for the 12th Games Will Be in Japan.

Havas, Garmisch, Germany, 16th: The International Olympic Winter Games concluded today. The closing ceremony was held in the ski resort, with no less than 100,000 participants. Führer Hitler attended in person and sat on the podium. Important officials of the Games were guarding his side. The audience cheered and paid their respects when they saw the Führer in person. Soon after, the award ceremony was held. The winning athletes from various countries were lined up in front of the podium, and the flags were flying. The flags of the top three countries in each event were raised on the Olympic flagpole in order, and the national anthems of those countries were played at the same time. Bela, the chairman of the International Olympic Committee, awarded the prizes one by one. Then, Hartel, the chairman of the German Olympic Committee, tied the commemorative ribbon of this Winter Games to the national flags of the participating countries. Finally, Bela gave the closing remarks, first thanking Führer Hitler of Germany, the German people, and the authorities of Garmisch, and inviting athletes from various countries to go to Berlin in the summer to participate in the 11th International Olympic Games. At this point, the closing ceremony was completed, and the cannons roared. The Olympic flame that had been burning last week was also extinguished. In total, over one million people have visited since the competition began ten days ago, including no less than 800,000 people who purchased tickets to sit in the audience.

The Chairman Discusses the Next Games:

Havas, Garmisch, Germany, 16th: The Winter Games of the Olympic Games have ended. Count Bela, the chairman of the International Committee of the Games, is scheduled to leave for Japan on the 18th. He recently told a reporter from Hamburg that his mission is to investigate whether the 12th International Olympic Games in 1940 can be held in Japan. Italy and Finland had raised objections to the idea of holding the next Games in Japan. According to Bela, if the Winter Games program cannot be held in Japan, the northern part of the country has a harsh climate and many mountains, which can be used as sports venues. As for the long distance to Japan, it is not a problem. Previously, the 10th Games selected Los Angeles, USA as the venue. At first, it was thought that the distance was too far and that the participants would not be enthusiastic. However, when the meeting was held, the opposite happened. Not only did the number of participating countries not decrease, but the results were also very impressive, which shows that the distance is not a cause for concern. Moreover, the spirit of sports in Asian countries is developing day by day, and Japan's preparations will definitely have good results, which is beyond doubt.

Ski Federation Lodges Protest:

Havas, Garmisch, Germany, 16th: The International Ski Competition Federation recently held a meeting and decided that if the International Olympic Committee does not allow former ski coaches to participate in the competition, the Federation will refuse to participate in the 1940 International Olympic Winter Games. This resolution was unanimously approved by the representatives of various countries attending the Federation. Count Bela, the chairman of the International Olympic Committee, recently declared to a reporter that this resolution of the International Ski Competition Federation is impossible for the International Committee to accept. Based on this, it is possible that the ski competition in the 1940 International Olympic Games may be cancelled as a result.

Order from the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Education to Investigate Hygiene and Educational Facilities in Primary Schools 178

Directing County Education Bureaus to Order Schools to Comply

Recently, the Ministry of Education, deeming it urgently necessary to investigate the state of hygiene and educational facilities in primary schools nationwide to compile statistics, specifically designed a Primary School Health Education Survey Form and ordered all provincial education departments to instruct their subordinates to complete and submit the form. It is now learned that the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Education, upon receiving the order, has already dutifully copied and printed the form, distributing it to the education bureaus of each county with instructions for them to order all schools to dutifully investigate, complete, and submit the form for onward transmission. It is said that the aforementioned form is divided into three types: A, B, and C. Type A is to be completed by the principals of each primary school, and Type B is to be completed by the public school teachers or hygiene subject teachers of each primary school, whether junior or senior.

Children's Educational Novel

Little Men (Part 1) (7) (9) 188

— Original by Louisa M. Alcott, Translated by Deng Xiaocang

They were all there—Meg's parents, Mr. and Mrs. March, Aunt Tandy and Aunt Amy, old Mr. Laurence, now with flowing white hair and declining spirit, Mr. and Mrs. Bhaer, and the young scholar they nurtured, as well as many friends who came to pay their respects to the deceased. We imagine that the retiring John Brooke, in his busy, quiet, and simple life, had little time for making friends; yet now they came in droves—old and young, rich and poor, high and low; unknowingly, his influence had spread to them, his virtue still shone brightly, and the many good deeds he had done in secret rose up to bless him. The multitude of mourners and their grief beside his coffin were a more powerful eulogy than Mr. March could have delivered. There was the employer he had faithfully served for many years, the poor old women he had helped with his meager savings to commemorate his mother, his wife, whom he had given so much happiness that even death could not completely destroy it, his brothers- and sisters-in-law, who had deeply occupied a corner of their hearts, his young sons and daughters, who already felt the loss of his strong arms and gentle voice, young children, weeping for their kindest playmate, and tall young men, suddenly moved, paying attention to a scene they would never forget. It was a very simple ceremony, and very short; Mr. March had intended to express his admiration and love for his most respected son-in-law, but the old father's voice, which had been choked with emotion during their wedding ceremony, was now completely unable to utter a word. After the final "Amen" (Note), there followed a long, lasting silence, until it was broken by the faint sound of Chrysanthemum Sweeny sobbing upstairs; then, Mr. Bhaer gave an order, and the voices of the well-trained children burst forth together, singing a hymn, full of noble and unrestrained emotion, and others unknowingly joined in one by one, singing with all their hearts, feeling that their suffering souls had risen on the wings of the hymn, which combined both strength and gentleness, to a realm of peace.

(Note) "Amen" is the concluding word of each prayer.

Page 15

Special Medical and Pharmaceutical Supplement of Shenbao

The Urgent Need to Promote Rural Nurses (Part 2) 189

— Yin Jinquan

There are various opinions regarding the plan for implementing rural hygiene. However, many scholars in our country acknowledge that the only way out of solving China's hygiene problems is to adopt a public medical system. Indeed, implementing rural hygiene must be organized and obtain the maximum of hygiene facilities, ensuring that these facilities can be distributed to the rural areas throughout the country with the minimum of economic cost. Therefore, the rural hygiene administration in our country must be managed by the state, establishing a systematic organization from the central government down to the rural areas. Only then can the maximum effect be achieved with the minimum economic cost. This type of organization is also recognized by European and American scholars. However, this plan depends on the financial resources of the government authorities. Therefore, in this turbulent time of poverty and financial exhaustion, it is very difficult to make the ideal a reality. Consequently, some people have proposed that: "Who among those in the medical and pharmaceutical field does not have a compassionate and charitable heart, and a spirit of sacrifice to serve society? Since the plight of the rural areas is so dire, to relieve the suffering of the farmers, we in the medical and pharmaceutical field must lead by example and quickly go to serve in the rural areas." But how easy is this? Because the graduates of existing medical schools cannot shoulder the responsibility of implementing rural hygiene, either their qualifications are too high and their standard of living is too high; or their qualifications are too low and their purpose is to make a profit. Moreover, ordinary medical schools focus on treatment and pay little attention to prevention. At the same time, whether everyone has a compassionate heart and is willing to come to the bankrupt rural areas to serve is still a question. Even if we take a step back and say that there are people with such compassionate hearts who are willing to serve this bankrupt rural area, but relying on business will not be able to support their lives. Taking another step back, if there are a few doctors who can and are willing to generously provide free medical treatment, but relying on the free medical treatment of these few doctors to promote medical care to the rural areas is absolutely impossible, it is not a viable solution.

In this environment, the new term "rural nurse" has emerged in response to the needs of rural society. Looking at the meaning of this term, we know that it is different from the ordinary nurses serving in hospitals. The author believes that rural nurses are the vanguard of implementing rural hygiene. Judging from the various facts above, the author believes that the following three points for the training of rural nurses can be offered to those who are studying rural hygiene issues.

The selection of rural nurse talent should be done locally: The talent for rural nurses must be selected from outstanding individuals locally (junior high school graduates or equivalent qualifications), and they must pass the examination before they can be appointed. Because those who grow up in the local rural areas are the only ones who know the customs and habits and suffering of the rural areas, they will gain the trust of the farmers and be willing to work wholeheartedly.

The training of rural nurses should focus on diligence and frugality: To achieve the maximum effect with the minimum economic cost depends on the proper implementation, but a part of it still depends on the diligence and frugality of the implementers themselves. Therefore, the words "diligence" and "frugality" should be the most emphasized in the training of rural nurses. In this way, they will not easily be contaminated by the bad habits of the cities, and in the current difficult rural areas, they will be able to work hard and enable the farmers to obtain real new medical security.

The teaching materials for rural nurses should be tailored to the needs: Implementing rural hygiene does not require purely treatment talent or hygiene talent, and it is even more impossible to afford both medical and hygiene specialized talent. Therefore, the rural nurse curriculum should emphasize both prevention and treatment, so that they can not only implement hygiene work, but also be responsible for treatment duties. As for the allocation of curriculum time and all the detailed methods, you can refer to the "Zhenjiang Rural Nurse School," which was the first to be founded.

In response to social needs, Zhenjiang has already founded a rural nurse school. Other counties in Jiangsu Province may as well follow suit and strive to promote it, spreading from counties to provinces and covering the rural areas throughout the country, which is also a good way to implement rural hygiene. If scholars believe that it still lacks a system, then when the country is stable and the national treasury is rich, and the state organizes a systematic organization, this group of rural nurses will also be the most suitable and most needed talents when implementing the public medical system. After adoption, it can reduce the time required for talent training, and the implementation of the public medical system will also have a group of skilled and fresh troops.

We have said a lot above, so we may as well calm down and think about it. The extent of rural bankruptcy has reached its peak, and the farmers are suffering from poverty and disease day by day. The country still does not have a systematic organization for implementing rural hygiene. Under these circumstances, rural nurses are the most suitable for the needs of the rural hygiene cause. Therefore, the promotion of rural nurses should be urgently promoted, and it is hoped that those who pay attention to rural hygiene will discuss it.

Letter from the Shanghai Medical Association 190

To Whom It May Concern: Recently, some newspapers, under the guise of promoting medical and pharmaceutical knowledge, have extravagantly engaged in the art of disguised advertising, misrepresenting words and deceiving society, which has a significant negative impact on the future of national health care. In the future, to popularize proper hygiene knowledge, we plan to contact and cooperate with your newspaper and other publications, providing a platform for our members to publish articles, so that we can distinguish between right and wrong and correct the public's perception. We believe that your newspaper will also be happy to do so. We are sending this letter to you accordingly, and we hope that you will take it into consideration.

Sincerely,

Shanghai Medical Association

February 23rd

The Relationship Between Medical Trends and the Nation 191

— Shen Songnian

In our country, everything lags behind others. Although we are known as the earliest civilization, even preceding all other nations, with a long history of over four thousand years, according to the definite formula of evolution, the development of all endeavors in an early-civilized nation should be directly proportional – even progressing earlier than those nations with later civilizations. How could we know that the reality is the opposite? Although our country was the earliest to be civilized, the nation's position is now below all other nations. It has already fallen behind. Why would medicine be any different? Here, based on my limited insights, I have summarized several points for a brief discussion.

(A) The Restraint of National Thought

The emperors of the feudal era, in order to satisfy their imperial desires and prevent national rebellions, adopted the imperial examination system, using the eight-legged essay to restrain the thoughts of the intellectual class. Once thought was restrained, how could anything else be discussed? Medicine also could not progress because of this; everything was trapped in old conventions.

(B) Not Seeking Progress in Scholarship

In the medical histories of various countries, one can often see the progression from metaphysics to practicality. The trend of Chinese medicine was previously like the precedents of various countries, but later it ultimately did not seek progress in scholarship. Logically, the achievements that predecessors did not complete should be developed and completed by later generations. Only then would they not fail the painstaking efforts of the predecessors in their initial theories. Therefore, research and discussion are the sources of "development." Not seeking progress has a very significant impact on the obstruction of scholarship.

(C) Not Public, Keeping Secrets

All inventions come from the rational abilities of the insightful and prescient. Once something is discovered, tireless efforts are made to research it. When one's abilities are insufficient, it should be publicly announced for everyone to study and discuss. After combining the wisdom of many and continuous research and experimentation, great achievements can be completed! However, the people of our country only know selfishness and self-interest. Whenever something is invented, they must keep it secret so that no one else knows. This is due to the fact that the government has had no appropriate methods to reward inventors since ancient times. Therefore, since inventors have no legal protection, they are naturally unwilling to make public announcements. An example can be given as follows:

For example, a martial arts instructor has one hundred sets of boxing techniques, but only transmits ninety-nine sets to his favorite disciple, because he fears that if the disciple knows everything, his skills will be equal to his own. With this thought in everyone's mind, it is passed down generation after generation of disciples and descendants, becoming less and less, and eventually lost. Medicine is also like this, so there is no progress.

(D) Mutual Infighting Among Colleagues

This is also selfishness and self-interest. For the sake of fame and profit, they do not hesitate to damage the reputations of colleagues. There is no spirit of mutual assistance, no mutual connection, and no discussion of academic progress. They even take pleasure in jealousy among peers. The benefits of mutual learning are lost, so how can medicine progress?

Understanding the above points allows one to glimpse the reasons why medicine in our country is not progressing. Although the direct cause of decline is due to the various oppressions of imperialists, we must know that if a country can strengthen itself, imperialists naturally dare not despise and invade it. For example, before the Meiji Restoration in Japan, everything was immature. The weakness of the country and the invasion of foreign powers were just like our country now. After the Restoration, they turned weakness into strength and were able to leap to become a world-class power. Just in terms of medical and pharmaceutical undertakings, they adopted Dutch medicine in the past, but after the Restoration, they abandoned Dutch medicine and studied new and progressive modern medicine. Therefore, they have already kept pace with the advanced countries of the world. This advantage of the Japanese people's inherent love of imitation is indeed admirable!

We can now know that not keeping pace with the world's trends, history has given us profound lessons, and in fact, it has already been proven that the result will inevitably lead to falling behind. The country will gradually decline, and even lead to extinction. Understanding this is sufficient proof that the prosperity or decline of a nation depends on the health of its people. To make the people healthy, it all depends on the popularization of medical knowledge, so that everyone understands the essential medical and pharmaceutical common sense and the necessary hygiene knowledge. This relies on the popularization of health education. Therefore, if we want China to survive in the world forever, we should study modern medicine of the world as much as possible, so that the progress of medicine keeps pace with the advanced countries of the world, and so that it is popularized to the people, so that everyone is strong and healthy, and every citizen has at least a little contribution to the country, or does a great cause that benefits the country. Because if the body is weak, the spirit is also depressed. This kind of person will never succeed in a great cause. It is sufficient proof that the success of a great cause depends entirely on a healthy body. The foundation lies in the development of medicine!

(E) The Evils of Stubbornness and Lack of Initiative

Some stubborn people criticize the study of Western modern medicine as wrong. This is a subjective view of those who do not understand the world trend. We must know that academics have no national boundaries. The strengths of other countries can make up for our shortcomings, as mentioned earlier. Sun Yat-sen said that we should catch up with all the advanced academic fields in the world, so as not to cause our country to lag behind, and the result is to reach the path of decline. This is a true and meaningful saying. For the sake of the practical interests of the country, for the sake of the true academic progress, Chinese and Western medicine should contact each other, unite together, and under the belief of science, jointly discuss academic progress. Because science is constantly progressing and inventing as long as it has not progressed to the extreme. If you think that past knowledge is already sufficient and there is no need for improvement, staying in place will make you fall behind in an instant. Those who fall behind are the harbinger of decline. If we want academic progress, the first thing is to understand the theories that only know what is happening but do not know why; break through those that cannot be understood, and develop the inherent materials that can be organized, extracting the essence and discarding the dross. This is also a step that should be taken.

For the sake of the country's practical interests and for the sake of mankind's lasting happiness, the aim should be to popularize medical and health knowledge among the people; gather medical talents in China, study modern medicine, complete the independence of Chinese medicine, and promote the progress of Chinese medicine at any time. Not only should it keep pace with the medicine of various countries in the world, but it must also embrace the ambition to produce new medical inventions like the advanced countries with scientific prosperity in the world.

Page 16

The facts have already proven that the laggards who drive the times backward, or those who stay in place, will not be eliminated by human effort; in the future, they will be eliminated by nature—just as the oil lamp is eliminated by the electric light, which is an ironclad proof that facts speak louder than words. "When palaces are built, cave dwellings are abandoned; when cooking is invented, eating raw food is eliminated." Everyone knows this, and it is the same as the above example. Now, in order to awaken those who are stubborn and do not know the trend of the times, I will go further and briefly describe the origin and development of medical history, so that the evolution of the times and the new trend of medicine can proceed, which is irresistible:

In ancient times, people's thoughts were simple and their knowledge was immature. They did not know what medicine was at all. When they encountered diseases, they treated them with the rational instinct of the insightful and prescient. The so-called rational instinct is like a dog that eats a lot of grass when its stomach is uncomfortable to induce vomiting; or like an ape that can pull out wooden or bamboo thorns from its body. - If they encounter something that cannot be treated with rational instinct, they just let it take its course!

Because humans, after all, have a brain that is more complex and larger than any animal, their rational instinct is naturally more developed than everything else. Therefore, the insightful and prescient philosophers later thought that diseases were strange, and that there must be gods, ghosts, and demons causing trouble there. So, whenever they encountered enemies, they held weapons (note: the weapons at that time were nothing more than sharp stones tied together, because the people's thoughts were immature and everything was simple at that time). They fought in the air over the sick person, thinking that they could drive away the gods, ghosts, and demons, and the sick person would get better. - This ideal treatment still could not cure the patient, so they thought that the gods, ghosts, and demons were more powerful than ordinary people and could defeat everything, so they immediately begged the gods, ghosts, and demons to release the patient, and then prayer came into being - just like Western medicine before it reached the realm of science, everything was controlled by monks. - This superstitious act still exists and is popular in large cities in China, and the ignorant and foolish people still believe in it very much. It can be seen that the new trend in medicine has not been popularized in the country at all, which is really lamentable.

The above superstitious acts still could not cure the patient, so the insightful and prescient Shennong discovered that herbal medicine could cure diseases, and after his continuous efforts, he used his own body as a test product. According to legend, he tasted the hundredth herb. He just happened to encounter arsenic, which could kill people, and sacrificed his life for it, which is really a pity! If he had known the composition of arsenic at that time, he would not have ended his life like this. Moreover, since he was the insightful and prescient creator, he must have had many contributions to medicine. He was the ancestor of Chinese medicine, and the current old medicine started at this time.

After that, there were many famous doctors such as Zhang Zhongjing, Bian Que, Hua Tuo, Ye Tianshi, ... etc., all of whom had a great influence on the progress of Chinese medicine.

However, the Chinese only know how to stick to old methods, do not know how to improve, do not seek progress, and do not know how to adapt to the new trend of science. The countries of the world are constantly researching, improving, and inventing, and constantly progressing, which has led to the current deformed state of backwardness in our country's medicine.

Before the new trend of progress is produced, because there is no equivalent to replace it, on the one hand, the natural trend, the old and backward, will inevitably be eliminated. This has been proven to us in history and cannot be denied. When something newer is produced, perhaps what is now considered new and progressive will also be eliminated by it. Thus, it is constantly progressing in an endless cycle. It can be seen that the trend of medicine also evolves along with the country until the end of mankind.

Understanding this is sufficient proof that those who lag behind the times will eventually decline and be eliminated sooner or later. In order to make medicine keep pace with the countries of the world and stand on the same level, I hope that all colleagues in the medical and pharmaceutical fields should study modern medicine at any time and follow the trend of the world. In order to prevent the old medical field from being eliminated by the trend of the times and for lasting happiness, I hope that the old medical field should move forward on the road of science together. That is the practical benefit of the country. However, there are also bad situations in the new medical and pharmaceutical field. Now I will copy what Mr. Chen Fangzhi said below. He said:

Academic discussion is not infighting.

Controversy over medical administration is not infighting.

Using position and power to try to eliminate other people's careers is infighting.

Those who are now in charge of health administration should also understand the trend of world medicine, and should not stubbornly think that studying in one country means that country can be a model, and that those who study medicine from other countries are not good. This has a great impact on the progress of the country.

In summary, we hope that Chinese medicine can become independent as soon as possible, and that the trend of Chinese medicine can progress with the new trend. It must rely on the joint efforts of our medical and pharmaceutical circles. It is definitely not that a part of the malformed development represents Chinese medicine. This kind of wrong concept must be eradicated in order to benefit the country. Medicine is related to the rise and fall of the country. This trend of progress depends on the unity of the medical community to jointly seek progress (end).

Regulation of Body Temperature 192

— Guo Renji

Dissipation of Body Heat When comparing the normal temperature of the body with the temperature of the air, the air temperature must be lower. Therefore, the heat on the surface of our body is constantly being taken away by the surrounding air. Also, during breathing, inhaling cold air and exhaling warm air also allows the heat to dissipate into the surrounding air.

Generation of Body Heat The implementation of life phenomena in the body never ceases. The heart continues to beat, and breathing never stops. Also, during eating, the digestive organs start working, and muscle movements are also performed. The result of all these movements is the generation of heat.

Regulation of Body Temperature When the Dissipation of Heat Increases When the method of heat generation in the body and the degree of heat dissipation to the surroundings can be appropriately implemented, the body temperature becomes normal. Now, because the outside air has become cold, due to the relationship between the body surface and breathing, the heat in the body is excessively dissipated to the surroundings, then the body temperature is in danger of decreasing. However, the body can create a large amount of heat to cope with it. If that large amount of heat is suddenly taken away by the surroundings, the body must urgently produce heat, which is the so-called cold shivering.

Also, in order to prevent the cold outside air from taking away the heat in the body, the skin blood vessels also contract; the skin becomes pale and presents a goosebump-like appearance.

Climate and Appetite In order to create too much heat in the body, the heat materials must be taken from a large amount of food. Therefore, when the autumn wind first rises and the climate suddenly becomes cold, the appetite naturally tends to be better day by day, and it is good to ingest foods rich in fat, because they can produce a lot of heat.

It Can Be Decided When Heat Generation Increases When Heat Is Generated In Excess In The Body Due To Some Reason. The Excess Heat Can Be Rapidly Dissipated To The Surroundings To Prevent The Rise Of Body Temperature. For Example, When Performing A Long-Distance Race, Excessive Heat Is Produced Due To The Movement Of The Feet And The Muscles Of The Whole Body. In Order To Rapidly Dissipate This Heat To The Surroundings, The Blood Vessels Of The Skin Expand And Appear Flushed, And The Heat Can Rapidly Escape From The Skin. Also, Because Water Vapor Cannot Be Rapidly Released From The Surface Of The Skin, The Work Of The Sweat Glands Is Particularly Diligent, And As A Result, Sweating Occurs.

The Determination Of Breathing Also Increases, Exhaling A Large Amount Of Warm Air And Water Vapor. Also, Like A Dog, It Often Sticks Its Tongue Outwards, Because Canine Animals Have Difficulty Dissipating Heat From Their Skin, And Rely On Breathing To Dissipate Heat. If You Look At A Dog In The Summer, Or After A Fast Run, It Often Stretches Out Its Tongue To Increase Its Breathing, Which Is Why It Increases The Dissipation Of Heat.

The Above Are All Things That Warm-Blooded Animals Do To Maintain Their Body Temperature At The Same Level. However, This Body Temperature Regulation Is Actually Controlled By The Thermoregulation Center In Their Brains.

Thermoregulation Center This Thermoregulation Center Maintains Its Body Temperature At A Normal Level In The Normal State. However, When Suffering From Infectious Diseases, The Toxins Of The Pathogenic Bacteria, Or The Products Of The Generation Of Their Toxins, Can Cause The Thermoregulation Center To Fall Into Abnormal State, And The Body Temperature Does Not Become Normal, But Often Becomes High. However, In The Case Of Sustained Fever Described Later, This Center Can Also Implement The Regulation Of Maintaining Its Body Temperature At A High Temperature.

Common Sense of Hygiene for Ear, Nose, Throat and Eye Diseases 193

— Tang Renjin

(78) The Relationship Between Syphilis and Nasal Diseases

Among nasal diseases, there are those that come from syphilis, called nasal syphilis. Nasal syphilis, like general syphilis, is divided into three stages. The stage with the most obvious and dangerous pathological changes is the third stage. It can rot the nasal bones, and the back of the nose becomes sunken. The so-called skylight, which is commonly said, also occurs in the third stage. Now, let me describe the three stages of nasal syphilis as follows:

First-Stage Nasal Syphilis The initial hard nodule produced by first-stage nasal syphilis is usually relatively rare. The initial hard nodules of the external nose mostly grow in the nostrils, forming superficial ulcers. The edges are mostly swollen and hardened nodules, the bottom is flat, and sometimes it invades the deep part and the surface. The initial hard nodules of the nasal mucosa mainly occur at the front end of the nasal septum, with the occurrence of reddish flat bulges. These bulges are prone to ulcers, the bottom is attached with dirty yellow or yellowish-white lard-like substances; and they are prone to bleeding. At the same time, there is swelling and tenderness of the external nose, and radiating pain in the head and lower eye socket area. The lymph glands under the jaw nearby also become swollen, and there is often fever and other conditions.

Second-Stage Nasal Syphilis Syphilitic papules on the nasal mucosa are usually rare, mostly a kind of erythema, the mucosa appears red, mostly on one side, and limited to the front. Although it does not present severe symptoms, its course is very long. As for the flat calluses that occur in second-stage syphilis, they mostly grow on the skin of the external nose and inside the nose. When growing on the skin of the external nose, spots with needle-head-sized bulges repeatedly occur on the skin of the nasal wing and nasal septum, appearing copper-red or brownish-red. The epithelium is partially peeled off and partially covered with yellowish-black-brown crusts. When growing inside the nose, it is prone to occur on the nasal floor and the front end of the nasal septum. Often the nipples proliferate excessively, causing the nasal cavity to become narrow. Sometimes the surface breaks and forms superficial ulcers. (To be continued)

Q&A on Dental Knowledge (20) 194

— Lin Jianxian

Chapter 6 Prevention of Dental Diseases

Section 1 General Remarks

(Question 102) Is the prevention of dental diseases highly valued in dentistry?

Answer Yes. In the past, so-called dental medicine was limited to the aspect of repair: specializing in how to treat dental diseases that have already occurred and restore the function of chewing. However, the perspective of modern dentistry has already tended towards the path of prevention, paying attention to the protection of teeth, the prevention of tooth decay, and viewing repair as a last resort. In fact, if dental diseases can be prevented, wouldn't that be a great happiness for mankind. The reason why I compiled this Q&A on dental knowledge is to enable ordinary people to have more knowledge of protecting their teeth.

(Question 103) Can dental diseases really be prevented?

Answer In principle, the teeth that nature has given us should not be damaged early. If we live a reasonable life from childhood, protect our teeth with appropriate methods, and do not mistreat them, then the teeth can definitely maintain their natural lifespan. Now, what the dental medical community in various countries is diligently researching is to find this appropriate and most effective method that can prevent the premature death of teeth and increase the oral happiness of mankind.

(Question 104) Has the prevention of dental health reached a successful stage?

Answer Although the research on the prevention of dental diseases does not dare to say that it is completely successful, we can faithfully implement various methods that are already known, as described in the following sections. Many dental diseases, such as tooth decay, can indeed be avoided or reduced.

Section 2 Oral Hygiene and Dental Protection for Children

(Question 105) What is the most important thing to pay attention to in preventing dental diseases?

Answer The most important thing to pay attention to is oral hygiene. Because tooth decay is caused by food debris, bacteria and acids in the mouth, in order to prevent dental diseases, we must first pay attention to the cleanliness of the mouth, wash away the residual food, and then try to eliminate bacteria and stop acids. At the same time, we must also take care of the training of teeth and gums. These can all be regarded as within the scope of oral hygiene.

(Question 106) When should attention to oral hygiene begin?

Answer It should begin from childhood. If the deciduous teeth are well protected in childhood, and a good foundation is laid, the teeth of a lifetime will not be easily damaged. Moreover, good habits such as brushing teeth can only be developed from childhood, so that they can be practiced unremittingly and benefit for a lifetime.

Standard soybean oil for both near and distant months rose by approximately two jiao.

Spot trading in yellow soybeans has slowed for Zha, Chi, Du, and Sha varieties, leading to a decrease in their trading activity. Prices in Shangzhongguan have fallen, while high-end prices have stabilized. Car soybeans are fluctuating due to market indecision in Dalian, causing corresponding shifts in the local market. As a result, the spot oil market improved by two jiao yesterday, while soybean cake sales were limited to scattered transactions, allowing prices to remain stable. Soybean oil mills are showing a slight increase in demand for yellow soybeans, with purchases of 700 bags of Jiehe soybeans and 1,300 bags of Zhumadian soybeans. Last Year's Foreign Trade (Cont. 2) 216

— Wang Jingshi

The largest increase in imports was in miscellaneous grains, which increased by 24,174,181 yuan. This was largely due to the import of foreign rice in the first half of the year. Foreign rice alone accounted for 23,877,908 yuan, while wheat increased by 3,018,083 yuan. Imports of machinery and tools also increased by over 65 million yuan, but imports from Shanghai have decreased. Imports of books, woven fabrics, and paper also increased by over 3.5 million yuan. The only significant change was an increase in imports from Germany, the United States, and Canada.

Export Trade 217

Export trade increased by 40,594,781 yuan. The main commodities responsible for this increase were oils and waxes, which increased by 25,615,141 yuan; textile fibers, which increased by 22,634,874 yuan; nut and seed kernels, which increased by 21,065,787 yuan; metal ores, which increased by 12,837,364 yuan; miscellaneous grains, which increased by 11,198,600 yuan; and animals and their products, which increased by 2,389,267 yuan, for a total increase of 87,741,033 yuan. Decreases were seen in piece goods, which decreased by 11,862,458 yuan; yarns and woven goods, which decreased by 11,862,458 yuan; tea, which decreased by 6,474,365 yuan; raw and tanned hides, which decreased by 5,479,040 yuan; sundries, which decreased by 4,600,402 yuan; and other textile products, which decreased by 1,724,018 yuan, for a total decrease of 42,065,072 yuan. The decreases were mainly in manufactured goods, while the increases were in agricultural products such as oils and nut and seed kernels. Analyzing the oil category further, tung oil increased by over 15.3 million yuan, with exports to the United States accounting for 12 million yuan. Peanut oil also increased by over 6.5 million yuan compared to the previous year, with the United States accounting for 5 million yuan. Cottonseed oil increased by over 2.2 million yuan. The increase in nut and seed kernels was primarily driven by demand from the United States. Of the 11.158 million yuan increase, the United States alone accounted for 7.8 million yuan. In the textile fiber category, cotton exports from China increased from over 15.3 million yuan in the previous year to over 21.7 million yuan. Exports to Japan were the highest at over 14.7 million yuan, followed by Germany at around 3.17 million yuan. Additionally, exports of raw silk also saw progress, with factory silk increasing from over 14.31 million yuan in the previous year to over 26.5 million yuan. Increases were seen in exports to both the United States and France. Metal ores saw a more widespread increase, with a total increase of 12.8 million yuan. Tin saw the largest increase, reaching over 6 million yuan, and there was a significant increase in tin granules. Miscellaneous grains increased by over 3 million yuan, purely due to increased demand for millet for Korean use. In the past, customs authorities did not require this type of commodity to be reported. Exports to Korea in the previous year were only 2,246 yuan, but last year suddenly jumped to 3,380,530 yuan, which is worth noting. Animal products, including hog bristles, eggs, and poultry, reached over 80 million yuan, an increase of 2.9 million yuan compared to the previous year. Exports to both the UK and the US increased.

Decreases were seen in exports of raw and tanned hides, which decreased by over 3 million yuan. The decrease in exports to illness (likely a typo, meaning "England") was similar to this amount, indicating a sharp decline in exports to the US. Tea exports decreased by over 6.4 million yuan, with the UK seeing the largest decrease at over 3.8 million yuan, likely due to the large amount of low-priced tea already available in that country, reducing the need for imports of Chinese tea. Tea exports to Soviet Russia also decreased by over 1 million yuan, while exports to Morocco increased by over 1.4 million yuan. Piece goods decreased by over 11 million yuan, mainly due to decreases in exports to Hong Kong (approximately 4 million yuan), the Kwantung Leased Territory (over 2 million yuan), Korea (over 1.7 million yuan), and British India (over 1.2 million yuan). The rest are omitted.

Trends in Trade 218

Analyzing China's foreign trade last year by country, the United States remained in first place, with a total trade volume of over 311.34 million yuan. Imports were valued at over 170 million yuan, with the main commodities being cotton, kerosene, timber, automobiles, steel, and machinery. Exports were valued at over 130 million yuan, with the main commodities being tung oil, nut and seed kernels, hog bristles, tea, and raw silk. Japan was in second place, with a total value of over 221.6 million yuan. Imports were primarily cotton cloth, sugar, steel, seafood, and rayon, while exports were primarily cotton, mineral ores, food, flour, hemp, and other similar items. The United Kingdom was in third place, with trade reaching over 140 million yuan. Imports were mainly machinery, woolen goods, and dyes, while exports were mainly egg products, followed by hog bristles and tea. Germany was in fourth place, with a trade value of over 132.2 million yuan. Imports were primarily steel, machinery, dyes, and chemicals. It is important to note that Germany's import value has actually surpassed that of the United Kingdom, and it may move into third place in the future. The percentage of trade volume accounted for by major trading countries is listed below:

Overall, while trade conditions in China last year were extremely difficult, there was a slight turnaround compared to the previous year. Imports gradually decreased, while exports of domestic goods slightly increased, resulting in a reduction in the trade deficit and a temporary easing of the negative trend. This is the first positive sign. Imports of commodities such as machinery, metals, and timber were significant and increased compared to the previous year, indicating progress in China's domestic construction efforts. This is the second positive sign. These are all encouraging signs that are cause for some satisfaction. However, the increase in China's exports was primarily in raw materials, while manufactured goods showed no improvement, indicating that China remains in a position of dependency. Furthermore, the increasing imports of grains, especially rice, highlight the ongoing serious problem of domestic food self-sufficiency. While China's foreign trade is showing signs of improvement, there is no reason for excessive optimism. To achieve genuine trade success, efforts must be made to strengthen the foundation of domestic industry and commerce, and government policies must be implemented to protect domestic industries. Only then can the future of trade be hopeful. (End)

Spring and Autumn

Tidbits 219

— (Maode)

Life is like sailing the ocean. It makes us understand that we have broken free from the stability of a fixed life, like a ship unanchored, and are floating into a world of uncertain life and death.

A tung tree's leaves will fall after some light frost, but a pine tree can endure the winter without withering because it has the spirit of perseverance. From this, we can understand that in our careers, we should not fear being surrounded by demons. As long as we have the spirit of perseverance, we will overcome everything.

If a person has determination and is willing to work hard, then they can rise from inferiority to high achievement, progressing gradually from near to far, and following the path to success step by step. But if they only aim high and far, indulging in pleasure and ease, they will forever hesitate in the graveyard of failure.

Zhuge Liang's Relics 220

— Mingyue

Zhuge Liang is a deeply rooted historical figure in China. Whether it's a small child or an old woman with white hair, the mention of "Zhuge Liang" immediately excites their interest in his "Zen-like wisdom and ingenious calculations." In the provinces of Jiangsu and Zhejiang, there is also a popular saying: "Three cobblers combined are equal to Zhuge Liang." And few people will misidentify "where Zhuge Liang was from" because Zhuge Liang's courtesy name was Kongming, not to mention calling him Mr. Wolong. In the Peking opera "Empty City Stratagem," there is also a line in the aria: "I am originally from the Wolong drawing..." Wolongtu is located fifteen li outside the east gate of Xiangyang County, Hubei Province today. It is not a remote place, but a very beautiful one. The shape of the mountain is not steep, but it is magnificent. The area is not very large, but it is very comfortable. There are winding paths and lush trees, making it a scenic spot. There is a pavilion on the map, which is the Baoxi Pavilion. Behind the pavilion is the Wuhou Temple, which houses the statue of Zhuge Liang. A Taoist priest presides over the incense and candle affairs. The temple houses two ancient relics: a pair of boots and an iron bowl. If visitors are willing to donate some incense money, they can ask the Taoist priest to take them out for viewing. The boots are made of cloth, but they are more than twice the size of ordinary boots. Their gray-black color indicates that they are indeed ancient relics from a long time ago. It is said that these were the boots worn by Zhuge Liang at the time. The iron bowl has a diameter of about one foot and a height of about eight inches. It is said that this was the bowl Zhuge Liang used to hold rice. Whether these are just fanciful stories, I am not an expert in antiquities and cannot say for sure.

Number Thirteen 221

— Zhou Xian

Although thirteen is said to be an unlucky number, my neighbor "Number Thirteen" is an exception and particularly popular.

The reason why this "Number Thirteen" is so popular is very simple: it's because of a woman, a young woman, a beautiful and young woman, and also a top student at a certain girls' school, as well as the only beloved daughter of a wealthy businessman.

The reason why this girl became known as Number Thirteen is even simpler: it's because her residence is Number Thirteen of a certain lane. So when Number Thirteen was around ten years old, gossips gave her the nickname "Number Thirteen." Later, "Number Thirteen" gradually grew up, and the name Number Thirteen gradually became famous, gradually appearing on the lips of every young man in the lane. So two years ago, when Number Thirteen was fifteen years old, the Public Works Department revised the house numbers and changed her house number to Five, but although the old house number was no longer used, "Number Thirteen" seemed to live on forever, as immortal as heaven and earth.

The reasons why Number Thirteen is Number Thirteen have been described above, and readers should generally know the outline. Naturally, Number Thirteen has hair that is permed loosely all year round, with very delicate waves, curved eyebrows like willow leaves, a straight nose, black and white eyes hiding behind long eyelashes, lips like cherries, and a slender body with graceful posture. In short, she meets the most modern "standard."

Number Thirteen is not only "beautiful on the outside" but also "wise on the inside." She is currently a high school student, but she is already a candidate for university queen. The reason why she became a candidate for university queen is not because of her beauty, but because she earned it with her knowledge. Because in school, not only are all her subjects at the top of the list, but her excellent works are also published in school publications. Moreover, she has repeatedly won championships in essay contests and performance competitions. At the same time, she is good at singing English songs and can dance all kinds of classical dances.

However! Number Thirteen is different from ordinary women in one way: although Number Thirteen is seventeen years old this year, although she sometimes goes to social events, it's really strange to say that she has never had a secret phone call or a secret letter, except for formal social engagements. Every word, every action, is absolutely public.

Therefore, although she has the nickname "Number Thirteen", her reputation can truly be said to be flawless.

Little Western Paradise 222

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter 24: A Callous Husband Chooses Profit Over Beauty; An Ambitious, Healthy Man Ventures into the Wilderness

Bei Hai really felt that his words were too obvious, and while picking up his chopsticks, he glanced at him. He saw that he was composed, placing his chopsticks in the bowl and slowly picking at the dishes, his left hand holding his wine glass, ready to raise it or not, and he only wore a smile on his face. So Bei Hai laughed, "Today, I am entrusted by my relative to negotiate a deal. Let's leave this kind of joking for when we have time later. "Buying More" then picked up the wine pot and poured wine into everyone's glass, laughing, "Business and jokes go hand in hand. It doesn't matter. Let's talk about the business. To be honest, I don't think you two are asking for prices that are easily accepted by the owner. It's different with us. It's a bank investment. Once it's invested, because doing business, the bigger the capital, the longer the struggle, and the longer the struggle, the more money you naturally make." As he said this, he seemed very proud, just shaking his head. Then he continued. But despite saying such a long speech, Bei Hai didn't understand what he meant, only drinking wine and eating dishes, listening to him. Wang Baozang was even less likely to study economics. Now that he heard him develop this theory, he just sat up straight, holding the fallen chopsticks with his hand to align them. Or holding the wine cup to his lips, sipping a little wine. Buying More, hearing that everyone was listening quietly, continued, "Business people, since they are prepared to invest heavily, as long as the business they are doing is what they want, they will naturally not be stingy with money. So if these two pieces of land can be bought by us, then the prices you need are always negotiable." Bei Hai saw that there was still more than half a cup of wine in his glass, so he picked it up and drank it all, laughing, "If we tell those sellers exactly what Mr. Jia said, I'm afraid they will not only refuse to lower the price but will even raise it." Jia Duocai pressed his chopsticks on the table, turned slightly towards Bei Hai, and asked, "Why is that?" Bei Hai laughed, "If two people are fighting over a torn piece of clothing, then the price of the clothing must rise. What more for a piece of land." Jia Duocai said, "Do you two Mr. Wang mean you don't want to sell to us?" Bei Hai laughed, "We sell land, we only pick the rich, whoever pays the highest price, we sell to them." (404)

Talking About Fake Medicine 223

— Ai

Good medicine tastes bitter but is beneficial to the illness. This is certainly true, but taking medicine that is not suitable for the ailment can sometimes kill. Therefore, good medicine is still good medicine, but a good doctor can use it to treat disease, while a quack doctor can kill if he uses it without care. This author often sees advertisements for Western medicine in newspapers that state: "German-produced medicine is a holy medicine for all diseases," or "Invented by a great engineer after decades of painstaking effort," and the advertisements use all kinds of exaggerated descriptions. Their techniques of attracting customers are so effective that it seems there is no need to see a doctor if you are sick. Someone as ignorant as myself is certainly unable to prove whether they are genuine or fake, so this kind of suspicion has not been resolved to this day. Yesterday, I bought several copies of "Healthy World" from the Life Bookstore. In the second issue, there is an article called "Again, Telling the Sick," which relentlessly attacks the unscrupulous behavior of some people in the medical field. In the third issue, there is an article called "Made in Germany?", which reveals the truth about fake medicines that are mixed into shadow films. This not only completely dispelled my doubts from the past year or two but also increased my understanding of the world and made me realize that there are such harmful tricks in society. At the same time, it aroused great anxiety: if good medicine is not taken properly, it can be life-threatening, then the effect of fake medicines made out of thin air is, of course, self-evident. I think there must be many people who are deceived. In the opinion of the editors of "Healthy World," and I wish to tell you all through newspapers, adopt an attitude of mistrust towards these fake medicines, publicize it to each other, and prevent people from trying them. This is a method, even if a helpless one.

Local Customs and Gazette

The Abandoned Lunar New Year in Suzhou 224

— Zhu

Time flows away like water, and the abandoned Lunar New Year has passed in the blink of an eye. But of all the times of year, in these difficult and lean times, the abandoned Lunar New Year still has the most liveliness, and everywhere there are scenes that make people nostalgic, used to gloss over the grim reality. Now, let me write about some of the lively scenes in Suzhou during the abandoned Lunar New Year to show a glimpse of what it was like.

Door Birds 225

Among birds, there is a type called the Yellow-headed bird. Although its body is even smaller than a sparrow, its nature of mutual destruction is like the crickets among insects. At the beginning of the lunar new year, bird owners gather in tea houses, placing a half-table on two long benches by the window. Then, they put two Yellow-headed bird cages together, and the two small birds start fighting on the three bamboo perches inside. Often, they fight until their feathers fall off, yet they still can't stop. The winning bird has a silk paper flower inserted on its cage to signify victory. The most valuable of these consistently victorious birds can cost as much as three or four hundred yuan.

Monkey Show: "Dressed like a monkey but still a monkey," monkey shows have been a very early form of animal performance in our country. However, because the performers from Jiangbei only repeat a few old routines, monkey shows have become outdated entertainment, only appearing during the New Year to fool children. In addition to the main character, a monkey dressed in red, there is also a pug and an old sheep as supporting characters. The monkey's tricks include wearing masks, somersaulting, climbing tree forks, and spinning with a whip. The dog's tricks include jumping through hoops and racing. After the monkey and dog finish their act, the grand finale is the monkey riding the sheep. The performer leads the old sheep to a distance, then releases it to run. As the sheep runs, the monkey jumps onto its back, like a person riding a horse. After running three times, the monkey show ends. Although the technique is very simple, it is quite amusing to watch occasionally.

Dragon Lantern Twirling: During the Lantern Festival, with its fiery trees and silver flowers, it is said to be the time when folk light their lanterns. However, the lively scene of beautifully painted lanterns is rarely seen these days. Yet, the dragon lantern twirling still exists in a couple of places. The dragon lantern is made of sections of gauze, with a dragon head and tail attached to both ends. When twirling, a skilled performer can make it move smoothly and freely, soaring and turning, truly resembling a living dragon. When such a dragon lantern walks down the street, the person at the front beats the "N鬧元宵" gong (羅鼓正在月裏敲打的,人名鬧元宵). When shops on the street see the dragon lantern coming, some set off firecrackers to welcome it. The dragon lantern stops and dances when firecrackers are set off, waiting until the firecrackers are finished before moving forward. Therefore, the more firecrackers set off, the more lively the dragon lantern becomes, with the sound of gongs and drums, and the crackling of firecrackers, decorating the special scene of the Lantern Festival with the dancing dragon lantern.

Literary Riddles: Literary riddles, or "文虎," are word games in which scholars guess the meaning. This year, literary riddles are particularly active in Suzhou, with two places where lanterns are hung with riddles. One place is the Lejun Society in Gongxiang, organized by a group of old gentlemen including Yuan Jinqiu and Cheng Zhanjiang. Although the poetry strips are somewhat profound, some of the colloquial phrases are quite interesting. For example, "Young age, accepting disciples," which guesses "Little person, old head." "This year's Canal is not doing well," which guesses "Lotus flower, young master." "Embroidered red water caltrop under the skirt," which guesses "Small character" (Suzhou dialect for "child"). One word hits the mark, causing everyone to laugh. The other place is the People's Education Hall in front of the old school, but the riddles there are not very clever, such as "Not afraid of fire," which guesses "Wok." It is very much like riddles guessed by children.

The New Year scene in Suzhou is, of course, not limited to the above. However, times have changed. Besides burning incense for stars, eating Yuanbao tea, and visiting the Wumiao Temple on New Year's Day, in the past, the young masters outside the city gates would take their favorite prostitutes and ride around in decorated carriages on the road. Ten years ago, there was a lively scene of "cars flowing like water, horses like dragons." But in recent years, the money-spending young masters have become too few, and as for the prostitutes, public prostitution has not yet been implemented, and private prostitution is being strictly arrested. This trend of riding around in carriages has disappeared on its own. However, during the New Year, movie theaters everywhere are crowded with a large number of audiences, which is unusually lively, replacing the prosperity of the past.

Special Report by this publication

A Glimpse of the Congee Kitchen 226

— Ying Dai

Every winter, philanthropists in Shanghai, in addition to opening shelters for the cold, also routinely open congee kitchens. This year is, of course, no exception. The congee kitchen run by the Zhabei Charity Group is still on Liuying Road. I made a special trip to get up early one day and hired a rickshaw to go to Liuying Road to visit because I knew that the congee distribution time was set from 7:00 AM to 9:00 AM every day. If I went late, I was afraid I wouldn't see the turbulent crowd of refugees.

It was really scary! When the fortunate ones in the city are lying in warm quilts, having their sweet dreams, and still don't know it's dawn, the front of the congee kitchen on Liuying Road is already crowded with countless hungry people. Even if it's not 10,000, it must be at least seven or eight thousand people. Looking from afar, I could only see heads moving and the sound of people boiling. Among these people, there are men, women, old people, and even children. Everyone is holding a tin can, a broken washbasin, or something similar to hold the congee.

It is said that most of these people have been waiting here since three or four o'clock the night before because they are afraid that they will not get congee if they are late. If they squeeze to the front, they can go in first, get the congee, and come out earlier, so they don't have to worry.

Inside the congee kitchen, there are several large vats buried in the mud. Rice is poured into the vats by the peck and cooked. One side is the entrance, and the other side is the exit. Adults get three scoops, and children get two scoops. The people who come in have empty tin cans and washbasins, but when they go out, these things are filled with hot white congee. Everyone who gets congee will show a smile on their face and hold it out. Some sit on the side of the road and eat before they can leave. If someone is not careful and the container of congee is overturned, they will pick up the congee with both hands on the ground, regardless of whether it is mixed with mud and salt.

One batch comes out, and another batch goes in. The people who want congee keep coming one after another. It is said that an average of three or four thousand piculs of rice are burned every day. This year, the congee kitchen, like the cold shelter, also feels the reduction of philanthropists and the lack of funding. Therefore, no one dares to determine how long it will be run. One day, when the donated money is used up, it will be closed. This group of hungry people will disperse until the congee distribution period is over, and the next morning, there will be such a turmoil again.
